آقائے ماذون کے ہاتھ برابر قیمت یا کم پر کوئی چیز بیچی تو جائز ہے
قال وان باعه المولى شيئا بمثل القيمة او اقل جاز البيع لان المولى اجنبى عن كسبه اذا كان عليه دين على ما بيناه ولا تهمة فى هذا البيع ولانه مفيد فانه يدخل في كسب العبد مالم يكن فيه ويتمكن المولى من اخذ الثمن بعد ان لم يكن له هذا التمكن وصحة التصرف تتبع الفائدة فان سلم اليه قبل قبض الثمن بطل الثمن لان حق المولى فى العين من حيث الحبس فلو بقى بعد سقوطه يبقى فى الدين ولا يستوجبه المولى على عبده بخلاف ما اذا كان الثمن عرضا لانه يتعين وجاز ان يبقى خقه متعلقا بالعين. قال وان امسكه في يده حتى يستوفي الثمن جاز لان البائع له حق الحبس فى المبيع ولهذا كان اخص به من سائر الفرماء وجازان يكون للمولى حق فى الدين اذا كان يتعلق بالعين ولو باعه باكثر من قيمته يؤمر بازالة المحاباة أو ينقض البيع كما بينا فى جانب العبد لان الزيادة تعلق بها حق الغرماء قال واذا اعتق المولى الماذون وعليه ديون فعتقه جائز لان ملكه فيه باق و المولى ضامن بقيمته للغرماء اتلف ما تعلق به حقهم بيعا واستيفاء من ثمنه وما بقى من الديون يطالب به بعد العتق لان الدين فى ذمته وما لزم المولى الا بقدر ما اتلف ضمانا فبقى الباقي عليه كما كان فان كان اقل من قيمته ضمن الدين لا غير لان حقهم بقدره بخلاف ما اذا اعتق المدير وام الولد الماذون لهما وقد ركبتها ديون لان حق الغرماء لم يتعلق برقبتهما استيفاء بالبيع فلم يكن المولى متلفا حقهم فلا يضمن شيئا
ترجمہ اور اگر آقا نے ماذون کے ہاتھ برابر قیمت پر یا کم پر کوئی چیز نیچی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کی کمائی مثل اجنبی کے ہے جب کہ ماذون پر قرضہ ہو اور اس سے بیع میں کوئی تہمت نہیں اور مفید بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام کی کمائی میں وہ چیز آ جائے گی جو نہیں تھی اور آقا کوشی لینے کا قابو ہو جائے گا جب کہ اس سے پہلے اس کو یہ قابو نہیں تھا اور تصرف کی صحت فائدہ کے پیچھے گئی ہوتی ہے پھر اگر آقا نے مبیع اس کو سپر دکر دی شمن وصول کرنے سے پہلے تو شمن باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ آقاحق عین فی میں بحیثیت جس ہے اب اگر حق حبس ساقط ہونے کے بعد بھی آقا کا حق رہے تو دین میں ہے گا حالانکہ آقا اپنے غلام پر مستوجب دین نہیں ہوتا بخلاف اس کے جب شمن کوئی اسباب ہو کیونکہ وہ متعین ہے اور مال عین کے ساتھ آقا کا حق متعلق رہنا جائز ہے اور اگر آقا نے اس کو اپنے پاس روک رکھا یہاں تک کہ شن وصول کرے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ بائع کو مبیع روکنے کا حق ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ دیگر قرض خواہوں سے زیادہ حقدار ہوتا ہے اس طبیع کا اور یہ جائز ہے کہ آقا کے لئے دین میں حق رہے جب کہ وہ دین کسی مال میں سے متعلق ہو اور اگر آقا نے مازون کے ہاتھ اس کی قیمت سے زیادہ پر نیچی تو حکم کیا جائے گا ازالہ محاباة کا یا وہ بیع تو ڑ دے جیسا کہ ہم نے جانب عبد میں بیان کیا ہے کیونکہ اس زیادتی سے غرماء کا حق وابستہ ہے اگر آزاد کر دیا آقا نے مازون کو حالانکہ اس کے ذمہ قرضے ہیں تو اس کا آزاد کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں آقا کی ملک باقی ہے اور آقا ضامن ہوگا اس کی قیمت کا قرض خواہوں کے لئے کیونکہ اس نے تلف کر دی ایسی چیز جس سے ان کا حق متعلق تھا بایں طور کہ اس کو فروخت کر کے وصول کر لیتے اس کے شمن سے اور جو کچھ باقی رہتے ہوں میں سے اس کا مطالبہ آزادی کے بعد ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قرضہ اس کے ذمہ ہے اور آقا کے ذمہ بطور ضمان اتناہی لازم ہوا جتنا اس نے تلف کیا ہے تو باقی قرضہ ماذون پر جیسا تھا دنیا ہی رہے گا پھر اگر قرضہ غلام کی قیمت سے کم ہو تو آقا صرف قرضہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قرض خواہوں کا حق اسی قدر ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب مد بر مازون یا ام ولد ماذونہ کو آزاد کیا حالانکہ اس پر قرضے چڑھے ہیں کیونکہ قرض خواہوں کا حق ان کی گردن سے اس طرح متعلق نہیں ہوا کہ ان کو فروخت کر کے وصول کریں تو آقا ان کا حق تلف کنندہ نہ ہوالبند اکسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح فون وان باعه المولى ... الخ اگر آقا اپنے ماذون غلام کے ہاتھ کوئی چیز پوری قیمت سے یا نقصان سے فروخت کرے تو یہ بالا جماع جائز ہے اس لئے کہ جب نظام پر قرضہ ہے تو آقا اس کی کمائی سے اجنبی ہے اور اس بیع میں کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔ نیز اس میں فائدہ بھی ہے کیونکہ نام کی کمائی میں ایک ایسی چیز آ جائے گی جو پہلے نہیں تھی تو قرض خواہوں کا کوئی نقصان نہ ہوگا پھر آ قا اس سے پہلے
If the master sells something to the ma'dhun at the equivalent value or less, it is valid. He said: And if the master sells something to him at the equivalent value or less, the sale is valid because the master is a stranger to his earnings when he has a debt, as we explained, and there is no suspicion in this sale, and it is beneficial because something enters the slave's earnings that was not there, and the master becomes able to take the price after not having such ability. The validity of a transaction follows benefit. If he (the master) delivers it to him before receiving the price, the price becomes void because the master's right in the specific property is by way of retention. If after it falls, it remains as a debt, and the master does not become entitled to it from his slave, unlike if the price is a commodity because it is specific, and it is permissible for his right to remain attached to the specific property. He said: And if he holds it in his hand until he receives the price, it is valid because the seller has the right of retention in the sold item, and for this reason he is more entitled to it than other creditors, and it is permissible for the master to have a right in a debt if it is attached to a specific property. And if he sells it to him for more than its value, he will be ordered to remove the undervaluation or annul the sale, as we explained regarding the slave, because the increase is attached to the right of the creditors. He said: And if the master frees the ma'dhun while he has debts, his emancipation is valid because his ownership over him remains, and the master is liable for his value to the creditors; he destroyed what their right was attached to, as they could have sold him and recovered from his price. What remains of the debts is demanded after emancipation because the debt is in his (the slave's) liability, and nothing became obligatory on the master except as a guarantee for what he destroyed. So the remainder remains on him as it was. If it (the debt) is less than his value, he guarantees only the debt, because their right is only to that extent. Unlike if he frees a mudabbar or umm walad who are ma'dhun and debts have ridden them, because the right of the creditors was not attached to their persons by way of sale, so the master did not destroy their right, so he does not guarantee anything. Translation: And if the master sold something to the ma'dhun at equal value or less, it is valid because his earnings are like a stranger's when the ma'dhun has a debt, and there is no suspicion in this sale, and it is beneficial because something enters the slave's earnings that was not there, and the master becomes able to take the price whereas before he did not have that ability. The validity of a transaction follows benefit. Then if the master delivered the sold item to him before receiving the price, the price becomes void because the master's right in the specific property is by way of retention; if after the right of retention falls, the master still has a right, it becomes a debt, but the master is not entitled to a debt from his slave, unlike if the price is a commodity because it is specific and it is permissible for the master's right to remain attached to the specific property. And if the master kept it in his hand until he collects the price, it is valid because the seller has the right to retain the sold item, so he is more entitled to it than other creditors, and it is permissible for the master to have a right in a debt if it is attached to a specific property. And if the master sold it to him for more than its value, he will be ordered to remove the undervaluation or annul the sale, as we explained regarding the slave, because the increase is connected to the right of the creditors. If the master freed the ma'dhun while he has debts, his freeing is valid because his ownership over him remains, and the master will be the guarantor of his value to the creditors because he destroyed a thing to which their right was attached, in that they could have sold him and collected from his price. Whatever remains of the debts will be demanded after emancipation because the debt is in his liability, and only as much became incumbent on the master as he destroyed as a guarantee, so the remaining debt remains on the ma'dhun as it was. Then if the debt is less than the slave's value, the master only guarantees the debt because the creditors' right is only to that extent. Unlike if he freed a mudabbar ma'dhun or umm walad ma'dhunah while debts had accumulated on them, because the creditors' right was not attached to their persons in a way that they could be sold and collected from, so the master did not destroy their right and will not guarantee anything. Explanation: If the master sells something to his ma'dhun slave at the full price or at a loss, this is unanimously valid because when the slave has a debt, the master is a stranger to his earnings, and there is no suspicion in this sale. Also it is beneficial because something enters the slave's earnings that was not there, so the creditors suffer no loss. Then the master...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings concerning transactions between a master and his ma'dhun slave who is indebted. The key principles are: (1) When a master sells something to his ma'dhun slave at the fair market value or less, the sale is valid and beneficial. The master is considered a stranger to the slave's earnings because the slave's earnings are for the creditors. There is no suspicion here because the slave is not favoring the master at the creditors' expense; rather, the slave acquires an asset that increases his earnings. (2) If the master delivers the item before receiving payment, the price debt is void because the master's right of retention in the specific item falls, and he cannot have a debt claim against his own slave. However, if the price is a specific commodity, the master's right can remain attached to that commodity. (3) The master has the right to retain the sold item until payment is made, as he has a superior right of retention (haqq al-habs) like any seller. (4) If the master sells at more than the value, the excess is considered an undervaluation (muhabah) because it harms the creditors, so the master is ordered to remove it or the sale is annulled. (5) If the master frees the ma'dhun while he is in debt, the emancipation is valid but the master becomes liable for the slave's value (or the amount of the debt, whichever is less) as a guarantee to the creditors, because the master's act of emancipation destroys the creditors' right to sell the slave to recover their debts. The freed slave remains liable for any remaining debt beyond the value. (6) Special cases: For a mudabbar (deferred emancipation) or umm walad (mother of the master's child) who are also ma'dhun, if the master frees them while they are in debt, he is not liable because their persons were not subject to sale for debt recovery; thus the creditors' right was not attached to their persons in the same way. The passage ends with a clarification that the ruling on the master selling to the slave is unanimous.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is deferred until the master's death. Such a slave cannot be sold by the master.
أُمّ وَلَد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master. She becomes free upon the master's death and cannot be sold during his lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master sells an item to his indebted ma'dhun slave for double the market value, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) The sale is valid and the master keeps the profit.
B) The master is ordered to remove the overpricing or the sale is annulled.
C) The sale is absolutely invalid.
D) The master must obtain permission from the creditors.

Key Takeaway
Selling above value to a ma'dhun slave harms creditors and must be rectified; freeing an indebted ma'dhun triggers liability for the master, but this does not apply to mudabbar and umm walad whose persons are protected from sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Master Selling to Ma'dhun at or Below Value
Ruling on master's sale to ma'dhun with condition on above-value sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master selling to his indebted ma'dhun and identify the condition when the sale exceeds the market value.

Core Idea
Master can sell to his own ma'dhun even if indebted, as he is a stranger to the slave's earnings.

This lesson addresses a common situation: can a master sell an item to his own slave who is permitted to trade (ma'dhun) and is already in debt? The matn of Al-Hidayah rules that such a sale at or below market value is valid, with no suspicion of collusion. We'll unpack the rationale and also see what happens if the sale is above value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: master sells an item to his ma'dhun slave. The ruling: it is valid (jā'iz) if the price is at or below the market value.
The matn states 'وان باعه المولى حتى يستوفي الثمن جاز'.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is it valid? Because the master is a stranger to the slave's earnings (the slave's earnings belong to creditors), and there is no conflict of interest. The sale may even benefit creditors by bringing a new asset into the slave's possession.
The commentary says the master 'is a stranger to the slave's earnings'.
3
Consider the above-value case
If the master sells above market value, the favor (muḥābāh) must be removed or the sale cancelled, because the excess belongs to the creditors.
The matn says: 'ولو باعه باكثر من قيمته يؤمر بازالة المحاباة أو ينقض البيع'.
4
Conclude the conditions
The validity depends on the price not exceeding market value. If it does, corrective action is required.
This condition protects creditors' rights.

Source Text

تشریح فون وان باعه المولى ... الخ اگر آقا اپنے ماذون غلام کے ہاتھ کوئی چیز پوری قیمت سے یا نقصان سے فروخت کرے تو یہ بالاجماع جائز ہے اس لئے کہ جب ماذون پر قرضہ ہے تو آقا اس کی کمائی سے اجنبی ہے اور اس بیع میں کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔ نیز اس میں فائدہ بھی ہے کیونکہ ماذون کی کمائی میں ایک ایسی چیز آ جائے گی جو پہلے نہیں تھی تو قرض خواہوں کا کوئی نقصان نہ ہوگا پھر آقا اس سے پہلے اس کی کمائی سے ثمن نہیں لے سکتا تھا اور اب اس کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا۔

قوله فان سلم اليه .. الخ - اب اگر آقا نے ثمن پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مبیع اس کے حوالہ کر دی تو وہ ثمن باطل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ بیع کے بعد آقا اپنے ثمن وصول کرنے تک مبیع کو روک سکتا ہے اب اگر روکنے کا حق ساقط ہونے کے بعد بھی آقا کا حق باقی رہے تو اس مال عین میں نہیں بلکہ دین یعنی اس کے ثمن میں رہے گا حالانکہ آقا یہ حق نہیں رکھتا کہ اپنے غلام پر قرضہ واجب کرے بخلاف اس کے اگر ثمن بھی کوئی معین اسباب ہو تو آقا اس مبیع کو سپرد کرنے کے بعد بھی اس کو وصول کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ مال متعین ہے اور مال متعین کے ساتھ آقا کا حق متعلق رہنا جائز ہے پھر بطلان ثمن کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اب آقا اس کا مطالبہ نہیں کر سکتا ہاں بیچ واپس کر سکتا ہے۔
If the master sells to him until he collects the price, it is permissible because the seller has the right of retention over the sold item, and therefore he has more right to it than other creditors. And it is permissible for the master to have a right in the debt if it is attached to a specific asset. And if he sells it for more than its value, he is ordered to remove the favor or cancel the sale, as we explained regarding the slave. Because the increase is attached to the creditors' right. [The following Urdu commentary explains these points.]
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah followed by its Urdu commentary (sharh). It addresses the validity of a master selling an item to his own ma'dhun (permitted slave) who is indebted. The ruling: the sale is valid if at or below market price, because the master is a stranger to the slave's earnings and no suspicion of collusion exists. However, if the master delivers the sold item before receiving payment, the right to the price is voided (bāṭil) because the master's right to retain the item (haqq al-ḥabs) is lost. After delivery, the price becomes a mere debt, and the master cannot impose a debt on his own slave. Exception: if the price is a specific asset, the master's right can remain attached to it. If the master sells above market price, he must either cancel the favor (muḥābāh) or the sale itself, because the excess is linked to the creditors' rights.

Key Terms
ماذون (ma'dhūn): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade; his earnings are for creditors if he is indebted.
محاباة (muḥābāh): Favoring in price by selling below market or giving a discount; in this context, selling above market imposes a favor from the creditor's funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the master do if he sells an item to his ma'dhun for more than its market value?
A) The sale is automatically void.
B) The master must return the excess and the sale remains.
C) The master must either remove the favor (muḥābāh) or cancel the sale.
D) The master must seek the creditors' permission.

Key Takeaway
A master may sell to his indebted ma'dhun at or below market value, but if the price exceeds value, the master must correct it to protect creditors.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Effect of Delivery Before Payment to Ma'dhun
Ruling on delivery before payment and its effect on the master's right to the price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the consequence if a master delivers the sold item to the ma'dhun before receiving payment, and identify the exception when the price is a specific asset.

Core Idea
Delivery before payment voids the master's right to the price, unless the price is a specific asset (ʿayn).

After a valid sale, the master has the right to retain the sold item until the price is paid (ḥaqq al-ḥabs). This lesson examines what happens if the master voluntarily delivers the item before payment. The matn rules that the price becomes void (bāṭil) because the master's right was attached to the item, not to the slave's person. However, an exception exists if the price is a specific asset (like a particular commodity).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
After a valid sale, the master hands over the sold item to the ma'dhun before the price is paid. The ruling: the price becomes void (bāṭil), meaning the master cannot claim it.
The text says 'فان سلم اليه ... بطل الثمن' (if he delivers... the price becomes void).
2
Understand the reason: loss of haqq al-ḥabs
The master had the right to retain the item (ḥaqq al-ḥabs) to secure payment. By delivering, he loses that right. The price then becomes a mere debt, and the master cannot impose a debt on his own slave.
The commentary says 'لان حق الحبس سقط' (because the right of retention is lost).
3
Recognize the exception: specific asset
If the price is a specific asset (ʿayn muʿayyan), not a debt, the master's right can remain attached to that specific item even after delivery. So the price is not voided.
The text says 'اذا كان يتعلق بالعين' (if it is attached to a specific asset).
4
Conclude the consequence
In the default case (price is a debt), delivery voids the price. The master cannot demand payment but may rescind the sale and take back the item.
The commentary notes that the master can cancel the sale (فسخ البيع).

وان باعه المولى حتى يستوفي الثمن جاز لان البائع له حق الحبس فى المبيع ولهذا كان اخص به من سائر الغرماء وجازان يكون للمولى حق فى الدين اذا كان يتعلق بالعين ولو باعه باكثر من قيمته يؤمر بازالة المحاباة أو ينقض البيع كما بينا فى جانب العبد لان الزيادة تعلق بها حق الغرماء

تشریح فون وان باعه المولى ... الخ اگر آقا اپنے ماذون غلام کے ہاتھ کوئی چیز پوری قیمت سے یا نقصان سے فروخت کرے تو یہ بالاجماع جائز ہے اس لئے کہ جب ماذون پر قرضہ ہے تو آقا اس کی کمائی سے اجنبی ہے اور اس بیع میں کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔ نیز اس میں فائدہ بھی ہے کیونکہ ماذون کی کمائی میں ایک ایسی چیز آ جائے گی جو پہلے نہیں تھی تو قرض خواہوں کا کوئی نقصان نہ ہوگا پھر آقا اس سے پہلے اس کی کمائی سے ثمن نہیں لے سکتا تھا اور اب اس کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا۔

If the master sells to him until he collects the price, it is permissible because the seller has the right of retention over the sold item, and therefore he has more right to it than other creditors. And it is permissible for the master to have a right in the debt if it is attached to a specific asset. And if he sells it for more than its value, he is ordered to remove the favor or cancel the sale, as we explained regarding the slave. Because the increase is attached to the creditors' right. [The following Urdu commentary explains these points.]
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah followed by its Urdu commentary (sharh). It addresses the validity of a master selling an item to his own ma'dhun (permitted slave) who is indebted. The ruling: the sale is valid if at or below market price, because the master is a stranger to the slave's earnings and no suspicion of collusion exists. However, if the master delivers the sold item before receiving payment, the right to the price is voided (bāṭil) because the master's right to retain the item (haqq al-ḥabs) is lost. After delivery, the price becomes a mere debt, and the master cannot impose a debt on his own slave. Exception: if the price is a specific asset, the master's right can remain attached to it. If the master sells above market price, he must either cancel the favor (muḥābāh) or the sale itself, because the excess is linked to the creditors' rights.

Key Terms
حق الحبس (ḥaqq al-ḥabs): The seller's right to retain the sold item until payment of the price.
عين (ʿayn): A specific, identifiable asset (e.g., a particular horse, a piece of land) as opposed to a debt (dayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the master's right to the price survive after delivery of the sold item to the ma'dhun?
A) When the price is a debt.
B) When the price is a specific asset (ʿayn).
C) When the master did not intend to void the price.
D) When the slave consents to the debt.

Key Takeaway
Delivery before payment to the ma'dhun voids the price unless the price is a specific asset, because the master cannot create a debt for his slave.

Creditors' Options When Indebted Ma'dhun Is Sold
Creditors' remedies after sale of indebted ma'dhun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options creditors have when a master sells an indebted ma'dhun to a third party and explain the legal basis for each option using the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
Creditors may hold seller or buyer liable, ratify sale, or void it; their right attaches to the slave until debt is paid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a nuanced situation: a master sells a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) who is deeply in debt. The sale threatens the creditors' right to recover from the slave's person or value. The author explains the remedies creditors have, drawing on analogies with mortgage and usurpation. Understanding these options clarifies how Hanafi fiqh protects creditors' rights when the debtor's asset is transferred without their consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and initial situation
The passage involves three parties: the master (seller), the buyer, and the creditors of the ma'dhun (slave). The slave has debt that 'encompasses his neck' (yuhītu bi-raqabatihi), meaning the debt exceeds his value. The master sells him to a third party, and the buyer takes possession and hides the slave.
The phrase 'yuhītu bi-raqabatihi' is key: it means the debt is equal to or greater than the slave's entire value, so creditors' right covers his whole person.
2
Understand creditors' rights before the sale
Before the sale, creditors have the right to sell the slave themselves to recover their debt (istis'ā') or to seek earnings from him. This right is attached to the slave's person, like a lien.
This attachment is the basis for their options after the sale.
3
List the three options and their legal bases
The passage gives creditors three choices: (1) hold the seller liable for the slave's value, (2) hold the buyer liable for the value, or (3) ratify the sale and take the price. The first two are based on the seller and buyer destroying the creditors' right (by selling/delivering and by possessing/hiding). The third is based on subsequent ratification being like prior permission, analogous to a mortgagee ratifying sale of mortgaged property.
The options are mutually exclusive; creditors choose one.
4
Examine the analogy (qiyas) to mortgage and usurpation
The author uses two analogies: (a) mortgage: as a mortgagee may ratify the mortgagor's sale and take the price, so creditors may ratify the master's sale. (b) usurpation: if a usurper sells the usurped property and is held liable, then the property is returned due to defect, the usurper recovers the value paid. Similarly, if creditors hold the seller liable and the slave is returned due to defect, the master recovers from the buyer and creditors' right reverts to the slave.
These analogies show the principle: the right attached to the object follows it.
5
Analyze the exception when the price reaches creditors
The passage ends with an important exception: if the master sold with disclosure of the debt, creditors may void the sale only if the price has not yet reached them. Once the price is delivered to them (without favoritism), they cannot void it because their right has been satisfied.
This clarifies that the option to void is suspended until payment; payment extinguishes the right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان باعه المولى وعليه دين يحيط برقبته وقبضه المشترى وغيبه فان شاء الغرماء ضمنوا البائع قيمته وان شاء وضمنوا المشترى لان العبد تعلق به حقهم حتى كان لهم ان يبيعوه الا ان يقضى المولى دينهم والبائع متلف حقهم بالبيع والتسليم والمشترى بالقبض والتغييب فيخيرون فى التضمين وان شاء وا اجازوا البيع واخذوا الثمن لان الحق لهم والاجازة اللاحقة كالاذن السابق كما فى المرهون فان ضموا البائع قيمته ثم رد على المولى بعيب فللمولى ان يرجع بالقيمة فيكون حق الغرماء فى العبد لان سبب الضمان قد زال وهو البيع والتسليم وصار كالغاصب اذا باع وسلم وضمن القيمة ثم رد عليه بالعيب كان له ان يرد على المالك ويسترد القيمة كذا هذا قال ولو كان المولى باعه من رجل واعلمه بالدين فللغرماء أن يردوا البيع لتعلق حقهم وهو الاستسعاء والاستيفاء من رقبته وفى كل واحد منهما فائدة فالاول تام مؤخر والثانى ناقص معجل وبالبيع يفوت هذه الخيرة فلهذا لهم ان يردوه قالوا تاويله اذا لم يصل اليهم الثمن فان وصل ولا محاباة فى البيع ليس لهم ان يردوه لوصول حقهم اليهم
If the master sells him while he has a debt that encompasses his neck, and the buyer takes possession and hides him, then if the creditors wish, they may hold the seller liable for his value, and if they wish, they may hold the buyer liable, because the slave's right is attached to them so that they could sell him unless the master pays their debt. The seller destroys their right by sale and delivery, and the buyer by taking possession and hiding. So they have a choice in holding liable. And if they wish, they may validate the sale and take the price, because the right is theirs, and subsequent ratification is like prior permission, as in the case of a mortgaged item. Then if they hold the seller liable for his value, and then the slave is returned to the master due to a defect, the master may get the value back, and the creditors' right is on the slave, because the cause of liability has ceased, which is the sale and delivery. It is like a usurper who sells and delivers, then the item is returned due to defect; he can return to the owner and recover the value. Similarly here. He said: if the master sold him to a man and informed him of the debt, the creditors may void the sale because their right is attached, i.e., the right to seek earnings and collect from his person. In each there is a benefit: the first is complete but delayed, the second is deficient but prompt. By sale, this choice is lost, so they may void it. They said its interpretation is when the price has not reached them. If it has reached and there is no favor in the sale, they cannot void it because their right has reached them.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with analogy (qiyas) to a mortgage. When the master sells the indebted ma'dhun to a third party, and the buyer takes possession and hides the slave, the creditors have three options: (1) hold the seller (master) liable for the slave's value, (2) hold the buyer liable, or (3) ratify the sale and take the price. This is because the creditors' right was attached to the slave's person (they could sell him to recover debts). The seller destroys that right by selling and delivering, the buyer by taking possession and hiding. The ratification is like prior permission, analogous to a mortgagee ratifying the sale of mortgaged property. If the creditors hold the seller liable and later the slave is returned to the master due to a defect, the master can recover the value from the buyer, and the creditors' right reverts to the slave. This is analogous to a usurper. Additionally, if the master sold with disclosure of the debt, creditors may void the sale because it deprives them of the choice between seeking earnings or selling the slave. However, if the price has reached them and there is no favor, they cannot void it.

Key Terms
استسعاء (istis'ā'): The creditors' right to employ the slave to earn and pay off debts.
اجازة اللاحقة (ijāza lāḥiqa): Subsequent ratification of a sale, which is equivalent to prior permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the buyer hides the slave.
B) When the price has reached the creditors and there is no favor in the sale.
C) When the master informed the buyer of the debt.
D) When the sale was at market price.

Key Takeaway
Creditors of an indebted ma'dhun have three distinct options when the master sells him: hold seller liable, hold buyer liable, or ratify the sale; their right to void is conditional on disclosure and non-receipt of price.

Creditors' Options When a Master Sells an Indebted Ma'dhun Slave
Explains creditors' options when master sells indebted slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options available to creditors when a master sells an indebted ma'dhun slave, and explain the condition under which creditors may rescind the sale.

Core Idea
Creditors have three remedies against seller, buyer, or the sale price; rescission only if price not received and buyer informed.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a master sells his ma'dhun slave while the slave's debts equal or exceed his value. The creditors, who have a claim on the slave's person, are given specific legal remedies. Understanding these options is crucial for grasping Hanafi commercial law and creditor protection in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger condition
The slave must have a debt encompassing his entire value (dayn yuḥīṭu bi-raqabatihi). This activates the creditors' right over the slave's person.
If debt is less than value, creditors cannot sell the slave; they may only pursue earnings.
2
List the three primary options
The creditors may: (1) hold the seller (master) liable for the slave's value, (2) hold the buyer liable if he took possession and disappeared, or (3) ratify the sale and take the price from the buyer.
Option (2) requires the buyer's possession and disappearance (takhfiya).
3
Understand the ratification rationale
Ratification is valid because the creditors own the right to the slave's value; subsequent permission is equivalent to prior permission, as in mortgaged property.
Analogy to marhūn: mortgagee's subsequent ratification validates the sale.
4
Examine the rescission scenario
If the master sold the slave and informed the buyer of the debt, creditors may rescind (radd) the sale because their right to earn and sell from the slave's person is lost.
The mashāyikh conditioned this rescission: only if the price has not reached the creditors and there is no favor (maḥābāt) in the sale.
5
Trace the defect scenario
If creditors held the seller liable and later the slave is returned to the master due to a defect, the master may reclaim the value from the creditors. The cause of liability (the sale and delivery) is nullified.
Analogous to a usurper (ghāṣib) who sells a slave, pays value, then the slave is returned due to defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان باعه المولى وعليه دين يحيط برقبته وقبضه المشترى وغيبه فان شاء الغرماء ضمنوا البائع قيمته وان شاء ضمنوا المشترى لان العبد تعلق به حقهم حتى كان لهم ان يبيعوه الا ان يقضى المولى دينهم والبائع متلف حقهم بالبيع والتسليم والمشترى بالقبض والتغييب فيخيرون فى التضمين وان شاءوا اجازوا البيع واخذوا الثمن لان الحق لهم والاجازة اللاحقة كالاذن السابق كما فى المرهون فان ضمنوا البائع قيمته ثم رد على المولى بعيب فللمولى ان يرجع بالقيمة فيكون حق الغرماء فى العبد لان سبب الضمان قد زال وهو البيع والتسليم وصار كالغاصب اذا باع وسلم وضمن القيمة ثم رد عليه بالعيب كان له ان يرد على المالك ويسترد القيمة كذا هذا قال ولو كان المولى باعه من رجل واعلمه بالدين فللغرماء أن يردوا البيع لتعلق حقهم وهو الاستسعاء والاستيفاء من رقبته وفى كل واحد منهما فائدة فالاول تام مؤخر والثانى ناقص معجل وبالبيع يفوت هذه الخيرة فلهذا لهم ان يردوه قالوا تأويله اذا لم يصل اليهم الثمن فان وصل ولا محاباة فى البيع ليس لهم ان يردوه لوصول حقهم اليهم
He said: If the master sold him while he had a debt that encompasses his neck, and the buyer took possession and made him disappear, then if the creditors wish, they may hold the seller liable for his value; and if they wish, they may hold the buyer liable, because the slave's person has become linked to their right such that they could sell him, unless the master pays off their debt. The seller is a destroyer of their right through the sale and delivery, and the buyer through taking possession and causing disappearance. So they have a choice in imposing liability. And if they wish, they may ratify the sale and take the price, because the right belongs to them, and subsequent permission is like prior permission, as with a mortgaged property. If they hold the seller liable for his value and then the slave is returned to the master due to a defect, the master may demand back the value; the creditors' right reverts to the slave, because the cause of liability has ceased, which is the sale and delivery. This is like a usurper who sold and delivered and was held liable for the value, then the item was returned to him due to a defect — he may return it to the owner and reclaim the value. Similarly here. He said: If the master sold him to a man and informed him of the debt, the creditors may rescind the sale because their right — which is to have him earn and to collect from his person — has been attached. In each of these there is a benefit: the first is complete but delayed, the second is incomplete but immediate. With the sale, this choice is lost, so they may rescind it. They said: Its interpretation is when the price has not reached them; if it has reached them and there is no favor in the sale, they may not rescind it, because their right has reached them.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hidayah explaining the legal options available to creditors when a master sells a ma'dhun slave who has debts encompassing his entire value. The matn first establishes that the creditors have a right in the slave's person, such that they could sell him to recover their debt unless the master pays. If the master sells the slave without paying the debt, the creditors have three options: (1) hold the seller (master) liable for the slave's value, (2) hold the buyer liable for the value if he took possession and caused the slave to disappear, or (3) ratify the sale and take the sale price from the buyer. The reasoning given is that the creditors' right is attached to the slave (tahqīq al-ḥaqq), and the seller and buyer have each caused loss of that right. The permissibility of ratification is analogized to a mortgaged property where subsequent permission is like prior permission. Then the text discusses a scenario where the creditors hold the seller liable, but the slave is later returned to the master due to a defect. In that case, the master can reclaim the value from the creditors because the cause of liability (the sale and delivery) has been nullified. This is likened to a usurper (ghāṣib) who sells a stolen slave, pays the value to the owner, then the slave is returned to the usurper due to a defect — the usurper then returns the slave to the owner and reclaims the value. Finally, the passage addresses a situation where the master sold the slave and informed the buyer of the debt. Here, the creditors may rescind the sale because their right to have the slave earn and be sold from his person is lost. However, the mashāyikh (senior scholars) specified that this right to rescind exists only if the price has not reached the creditors; if it has, and there was no favor (maḥābāt) in the sale, they cannot rescind because their right has been satisfied.

Key Terms
مَأْذُون (ma'dhūn): A slave who is permitted by his master to engage in trade.
دَيْن يحيط برقبته (dayn yuḥīṭu bi-raqabatihi): A debt that encompasses the slave's value, meaning the total debt equals or exceeds the slave's market price.
غُرَمَاء (ghuramā'): The creditors of the ma'dhūn slave.
اَلْإِجَازَة اللَّاحِقَة كَالْإِذْن السَّابِق (al-ijāzatu al-lāḥiqatu ka-al-idhni al-sābiq): Subsequent ratification is equivalent to prior permission in validating a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hidayah passage, if a master sells an indebted ma'dhun slave and the buyer takes possession and disappears, which of the following is NOT a creditor option?
A) Hold the seller liable for the value.
B) Hold the buyer liable for the value.
C) Rescind the sale.
D) Ratify the sale and take the price.

Key Takeaway
Creditors of an indebted ma'dhun slave have three remedies when the master sells the slave, but rescission is conditional upon the buyer being informed of the debt and the price not having reached the creditors.

Three Options for Creditors When a Ma'dhun Slave is Sold and the Buyer Disappears
Explaining creditors' three choices when master sells indebted ma'dhun slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options available to creditors when a master sells an indebted ma'dhun slave and the buyer disappears, and explain the legal basis for each option.

Core Idea
Creditors can hold the seller, the buyer, or ratify the sale — their right is tied to the slave.

In Hanafi fiqh, a ma'dhun slave (permitted to trade) can incur debts. If the master sells such a slave and the buyer absconds, the creditors are not left helpless. The law gives them a choice: they can seek compensation from either the seller or the buyer, or they can validate the sale and take the price. This lesson explains the rationale and legal mechanism behind these options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their actions
The master sells the ma'dhun slave, the buyer takes possession and disappears, and creditors have a right attached to the slave.
2
Understand the creditors' right
The creditors' right is in the slave himself; they had the power to sell him to recover their debt, so the master's sale without their consent violates that right.
3
List the three options and the principle of subsequent permission
Option 1: Hold the seller liable for the price. Option 2: Hold the buyer liable. Option 3: Ratify the sale and take the price from the buyer. The third option is based on 'subsequent permission equals prior permission'.
This principle also applies in mortgaged property cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب المادون

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ ترجمہ اگر آقا نے مازون کو فروخت کر دیا۔ حالانکہ اس پر ایسا قرضہ ہے جو اس کی گردن کو محیط ہے اور مشتری نے اس پر قبضہ کر کے غائب کر دیا تو قرض خواہ چاہے بائع کو اس کی قیمت کا ضامن بنائیں۔ چاہے مشترکی کیونکہ ان کا حق غلام سے متعلق ہوا تھا۔ یہاں تک کہ ان کو اس کے فروخت کرنے کا اختیار تھا مگر یہ کہ آقا ان کا قرضہ چکا دے پھر بائع ان کا حق تلف کنندہ ہے بیچنے اور سپر د کرنے کے ذریعہ سے اور مشتری قبضہ کرنے اور غائب کر دینے کے ذریعہ سے پس تاوان لینے میں ان کو اختیار دیا جائے گا اور اگر چاہیں تو بیع کو جائز رکھیں اور ثمن لے لیں۔ کیونکہ حق تو انہی کا ہے ادا جازت لاحقہ مثل اجازت سابقہ ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے مال مرہون ہوتا ہے۔
Book of Al-Ma'dhun. Ashraf Al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. Translation: If the master sold the ma'dhun slave, while he has a debt that encompasses his neck, and the buyer took possession and made him disappear, then the creditors may either make the seller liable for his price, or make the buyer liable, because their right was attached to the slave, so much so that they had the right to sell him, unless the master pays off their debt. Then the seller is the violator of their right through selling and delivering, and the buyer through taking possession and making disappear. So they will be given a choice in taking compensation. And if they wish, they may ratify the sale and take the price, because the right is exclusively theirs; subsequent permission becomes like prior permission, as with mortgaged property.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It deals with the case where a master sells his ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) while the slave has debts that encircle his value. If the buyer takes possession and then disappears (making the slave unavailable), the creditors have three options: (1) They can claim the price from the seller (the master), because the master violated their right by selling the slave. (2) They can claim from the buyer, because the buyer violated by taking possession and then causing the slave to disappear. (3) They can ratify the sale and take the price from the buyer; their subsequent permission validates the sale retroactively, just as in the case of mortgaged property where the mortgagee's subsequent permission validates the sale. The text emphasizes that the creditors' right is in the slave himself, so they have full authority.

Key Terms
ماذون (ma'dhun): A slave whom the master has given permission to engage in trade.
تضمین (tadmeen): Making someone liable for compensation (the price) due to violation.
اجازت لاحقہ (ijaazat lahiqah): Subsequent permission that retroactively validates an act, similar to prior permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a ma'dhun slave with encompassing debts is sold and the buyer disappears, what options do creditors have?
A) Only sue the seller
B) Only sue the buyer
C) Sue seller, sue buyer, or ratify the sale
D) Only cancel the sale

Key Takeaway
Creditors of a ma'dhun slave have three choices when the slave is sold and the buyer disappears: hold the seller, hold the buyer, or ratify the sale.

Recovering Price After Slave Returned Following Compensation
Detailing seller's right to recover price if slave returned after compensation paid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the return of price when a sold slave is returned after creditors have taken compensation, and explain the underlying qiyas with the usurper case.

Core Idea
If creditors took compensation for the slave, but the slave is returned due to defect, the master recovers the price and creditors' right reverts to the slave.

This lesson addresses a nuanced scenario in sale: when a slave is sold, creditors take compensation from the master, then the slave is returned due to a defect. The Hanafi school applies qiyas to the case of a usurper to determine that the master can reclaim the price. Understanding this rule clarifies how compensation rights are undone when the basis for compensation is removed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
Understand the starting point: a slave is sold, and creditors of the buyer take compensation from the seller (master) for the value of the slave.
The compensation is taken as a guarantee for the slave's loss due to the buyer's debt.
2
Identify the event triggering recovery
The slave is later returned to the master due to a discovered defect. This return nullifies the basis for the compensation.
The return is due to a defect, not a voluntary return.
3
Understand the legal consequence
The master can take back the price from the creditors, and the creditors' right reverts to the slave itself.
The cause of compensation (sale and delivery) is gone, so the compensation is undone.
4
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The ruling is analogized to a usurper who sells a usurped slave, becomes liable for the price, then the slave is returned to him due to a defect. The usurper can then return the slave to the owner and reclaim the price he paid as compensation.
Both cases involve a party receiving compensation for a slave, then the slave returns, voiding the basis for compensation.
5
Apply the rule to creditors
Just as the usurper's liability reverses, the creditors' compensation is reversed. The master recovers the price, and creditors' right reattaches to the slave.
This ensures that the master is not unjustly deprived of both slave and price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اب اگر انہوں نے بائع سے اس کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لیا پھر وہ کسی عیب کی وجہ سے آقا کو واپس کر دیا گیا تو آقا قیمت واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ پس غرماء کا حق غلام میں ہو جائے گا کیونکہ تاوان کا سبب زائل ہو گیا اور وہ بیچنا اور سپر د کرنا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے غاصب نے بیچ کر سپر د کیا اور قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا پھر بوجہ عیب اس کو واپس کر دیا تو وہ پالک کو واپس کر کے قیمت واپس لے سکتا ہے۔
Now if they took compensation for its price from the seller, then the slave was returned to the master due to some defect, the master can take back the price. Then the creditors' right will be in the slave, because the cause of compensation—which is selling and delivering—has been removed. And this is like the case where a usurper sold and delivered a usurped slave and became liable for the price, then the slave was returned to him due to a defect; then he can return it to the owner and take back the price.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that explains what happens if the creditors choose to take compensation from the seller (the master) and later the slave is returned to the master due to a defect. The ruling: the master can recover the price from the creditors because the basis for their compensation—the wrongful sale and delivery—is voided by the return. Consequently, the creditors' right reverts to the slave itself. This is analogized to a usurper who sells a usurped slave, becomes liable for the price, but then the slave is returned to him due to a defect; the usurper can then return the slave to the owner and reclaim the price he paid as compensation. So the creditors' original right in the slave is restored.

Key Terms
تاوان (tawaan): Compensation/indemnity paid for the loss of the slave due to wrongful act.
غاصب (ghaasib): Usurper who wrongfully takes possession of another's property.

C) Master can take back the price from creditors, and creditors' right reverts to the slave

Creditors' Right to Cancel Sale When Debt Notified
Explaining creditors' option to cancel sale when master sells with disclosure of debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which creditors lose their right to cancel the sale of a ma'dhun slave and explain the reasoning of the Mashayikh.

Core Idea
Creditors can cancel a notified sale only if they have not yet received the price—disclosure does not extinguish their right.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explores the creditors' right to rescind the sale of a slave who owes debts. The master sells the slave, informing the buyer of the debt, yet the creditors retain the option to cancel. Why? Because their right to full recovery might be better served by the slave working off the debt (sa'ayah) rather than a possibly deficient immediate payment. However, later Hanafi jurists (Mashayikh) restrict this right: it exists only if the creditors have not yet received the sale price. Let's unpack the logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its ruling
The master sells a ma'dhun slave and informs the buyer of the slave's debt. The creditors have the right (khiyar) to cancel the sale. This sale is valid but subject to rescission.
2
Determine the condition for the cancellation right
The text states that creditors can cancel because their right is attached. But the Mashayikh clarify: this right exists only if the creditors have not yet received the sale price. If they have received the price and no favoritism occurred, they cannot cancel.
Condition: receipt of price extinguishes the right.
3
Analyze the underlying rationale
The creditors have two methods to recover: (1) force the slave to earn (sa'ayah) – which yields the full debt but is deferred, (2) collect from the sale price – which is immediate but may be less. By selling, the master removes the first option, so creditors can cancel to preserve it.
The right protects the possibility of full recovery.
4
Apply the Mashayikh's ta'wil
The original text seems to grant cancellation unconditionally. The Mashayikh interpret it as conditional on non-receipt of price. This ta'wil reconciles the text with the principle that creditors should not unjustly cancel after receiving their due.
Ta'wil narrows the ruling.
5
State the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position: creditors can cancel the sale only if they have not yet received the price. If they have received it, they have no right to cancel.
This is the fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اس قرضہ سے آگاہ کر دیا تو غرماء کو بیع رد کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کا حق متعلق ہے اور وہ کمائی کرانا اور اس کی گردن سے وصول کرنا ہے۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک میں فائدہ ہے مگر مؤخر ہے اور دوسرا فائدہ ناقص ہے مگر معجل ہے اور فروخت کرنے میں یہ اختیار فوت ہو جاتا ہے اسی لئے وہ بیع کو رد کر سکتے ہیں۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ غر ما، کوشن وصول نہیں ہوا۔ اگر ہو چکا اور بیچ میں کوئی محابات نہیں ہے تو اب بیع رد نہیں کر سکتے ۔ کیونکہ ان کو ان کا حق پہنچ گیا۔
And if he informed [the buyer] of this debt, then the creditors have the option to cancel the sale. Because their right is attached, and it is [the right] to make him earn and to collect from his neck. And in each of these there is a benefit, but one is deferred and the other deficient but immediate. And with the sale, this option is lost, therefore they can cancel the sale. The Mashayikh said that its interpretation is that the creditors' price has not been received. If it has been received and there is no rebate [favor] in the sale, then now they cannot cancel the sale, because they have received their right.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage explains that even if the master informs the buyer of the slave's debt at the time of sale, the creditors still have the right to cancel the sale. The reason is that their right is attached to the slave, and the owner could either have the slave earn money (sa'ayah) to pay off the debt gradually, or sell the slave and pay from his value. Earning provides full payment but delayed; immediate sale may be less but quick. By selling, the master removes the earning option. Hence creditors can cancel the sale to protect their interest. However, the Mashayikh (later scholars) clarify that this cancellation right exists only if the creditors have not yet received the price from the sale. If they have already received the price (and there is no favoritism in the sale), they cannot cancel because their right is fulfilled.

Key Terms
سعایت (sa'ayah): Earning by the slave to pay off his debts.
رد بیع (radd al-bay'): Cancellation/annulment of the sale by creditors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition do creditors lose their right to cancel the sale of a ma'dhun slave?
A) When the buyer knew of the debt
B) When the creditors have already received the sale price
C) When the master sells at a fair price
D) When the slave is returned

Key Takeaway
Creditors can cancel the sale only if they have not yet received the price; once they receive it, the right is lost.

Creditors' Right to Rescind Sale of a Ma'dhun Slave
Explains creditors' rescission right and effect of debt disclosure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which creditors of a ma'dhun slave may rescind the sale and identify when the option is lost.

Core Idea
Creditors can rescind sale of ma'dhun slave only if the price hasn't reached them and no favoritism exists.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the legal position regarding the sale of a ma'dhun slave who is in debt. The creditors have a choice: seek repayment through the slave's earnings (sa'ayah) or seize his person. When the master sells the slave, the sa'ayah option is lost, so creditors gain the right to rescind the sale. Understanding this option is essential for those involved in trade with ma'dhun slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their rights
List the master, slave (ma'dhun), creditors, and buyer. Note that the creditors have a right related to the slave's person and earnings.
2
Understand the creditors' two options before sale
Creditors may either demand the slave work to repay (sa'ayah) or take possession of his person. Each has pros and cons.
Sa'ayah recovers full debt slowly; person seizure is immediate but may recover less.
3
Analyze the effect of the sale on these options
The sale eliminates the sa'ayah option because the slave is no longer under the master's control. Therefore, creditors gain the right to rescind the sale to restore their original options.
4
Examine the effect of informing the buyer of the debt
If the master discloses the debt to the buyer, the buyer forfeits his right to return the slave due to the defect of indebtedness. However, the creditors' rescission right remains if the price is insufficient for their debts.
The sale is binding between buyer and seller but not necessarily on creditors.
5
Apply the mashayikh's interpretation
The creditors' option to rescind exists only if the price has not been received by them. If they have received the price and there is no favoritism in the sale, they are deemed satisfied and lose the option.
Receipt of price implies approval of the sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو كان المولى الخ - آقا نے دین جتا کر عبد ماذون کی بیع کی اور مشتری کو دین کا اقرار ہے۔ تو قرض خواہوں کو ر د بیع میں اختیار ہے اس واسطے کہ ان کا حق غلام سے متعلق ہے کہ وہ چاہیں غلام سے سعایت کرالیں اور چاہیں تو اس کی ذات سے وصول کر لیں ۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک میں فائدہ ہے سعایت یعنی کمائی کرانے میں تو فائدہ یہ ہے کہ پورا قرضہ وصول ہوتا ہے۔ مگر تاخیر کے ساتھ اور ذات غلام سے وصول کرنے میں فائدہ یہ ہے کہ قرضہ فی الحال وصول ہو جاتا ہے لیکن اس احتمال کے ساتھ کہ ممکن ہے کم وصول ہو اور جب آقا نے اس کو فر وخت کر دیا تو ان کا یہ اختیار فوت ہو گیا۔ یعنی کمائی کرانا باقی نہیں رہا لہذا ان کو رد بیع کا اختیار ہے۔ قوله واعلمه بالدین الخ - یعنی آقا نے غلام فروخت کرتے وقت مشتری کو بتلا دیا کہ جو غلام میں تیرے ہاتھ فروخت کر رہا ہوں وہ مقروض ہے۔ اس اعلام کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ عیب دین کی وجہ سے روبیع کا جو اختیار مشتری کو حاصل ہوتا ہے وہ ساقط ہو جائے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ بیچ ، بائع ومشتری کے درمیان لازم واقع ہوگی گوغر ماء کے حق میں لازم نہ ہو (اذا لم يكن في ثمنه وفاء بديونهم) قوله قالو اتأويله الخ - مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ ربیع کا اختیار اس وقت ہے جب غلام کا شمن قرض خواہوں کے پاس نہ پہنچا ہو اور اگر شمن وصول ہو چکا اور بیع میں کوئی محابات بھی نہیں ہے تور دبیع کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان کا شمن پر قبضہ کر بیع سے راضی ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
He said, 'And if the master...' - The master sold a ma'dhun slave while the debt remained, and the buyer acknowledges the debt. So the creditors have the option to rescind the sale because their right is related to the slave: they may either seek earnings (sa'ayah) from the slave or recover from his person. Each has a benefit: in seeking earnings, the entire debt is recovered but with delay; in recovering from his person, the debt is recovered immediately but possibly less. When the master sold him, their option of seeking earnings is lost, so they have the option to rescind. He said, 'And he informed him of the debt...' - The master at the time of sale informed the buyer that the slave is indebted. The benefit of this notification is that the buyer's option due to the defect of debt is dropped, and the sale becomes binding between seller and buyer, though not binding regarding the creditors (if the price is insufficient for their debts). He said, 'They said: its interpretation...' - The mashayikh said the interpretation is that the option to rescind is when the slave's price has not reached the creditors; if the price has been received and there is no favoritism in the sale, then there is no option to rescind, because their receipt of the price is evidence of their approval of the sale.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) who is in debt. The master sells the slave while the buyer acknowledges the debt. The creditors have the option to rescind the sale because their right pertains to the slave: they could either have the slave work to repay (sa'ayah) or seize his person. The sale eliminates the sa'ayah option, so they can rescind. If the master informs the buyer of the debt, the buyer loses his option to return the slave due to the defect of indebtedness, but the creditors still have their option if the price does not cover their debts. The mashayikh interpret that the creditors' option exists only if the price hasn't reached them; if it has, they are deemed satisfied.

Key Terms
عبد مأذون (abd ma'dhun): A slave who is permitted by his master to engage in trade.
سعایت (sa'ayah): The creditors' right to have the slave work to pay off the debt.
رد بیع (radd al-bay'): The option to rescind the sale, returning the slave and recovering the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) When the slave is a non-ma'dhun slave
D) When the master is present

Key Takeaway
Creditors of a ma'dhun slave can rescind the sale only if the price is insufficient and not yet received, with no favoritism.

The Buyer as a Valid Opponent When Seller Is Absent: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute over buyer being a valid opponent for creditors when seller is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf on whether the buyer is a valid opponent (khasm) when the seller is absent, explain the reasoning behind each position, and apply the same principle to the analogous case of shuf'ah (pre-emption) and gifts.

Core Idea
The buyer cannot be a khasm for claims requiring rescission of the sale, because that would judge the absent seller; ownership claim alone is insufficient.

When a seller absconds after a sale, can creditors sue the buyer directly? The Hanafi school splits: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) says no, because the claim would void the contract and affect the absent seller. Imam Abu Yusuf says yes, because the buyer claims ownership. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its application to similar cases like shuf'ah and gifts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Read the passage to identify the exact legal question: when the seller is absent and the buyer denies the debt, can the creditors (ghurama) litigate against the buyer?
The dispute hinges on whether the buyer is a valid opponent (khasm) for a claim that effectively requires rescission of the sale (faskh al-'aqd).
2
State the Two Positions
Identify the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad – 'the two sides') and the opposing opinion (Abu Yusuf). Note the thamarah al-khilaf: under the majority view, creditors must wait for the seller; under Abu Yusuf, they can proceed immediately.
The passage also extends this to the shuf'ah case: if a buyer gifts the property and then disappears, the donee is not a khasm for the pre-emptor.
3
Analyze the Proofs (Istidlal)
For the two sides: the claim includes rescission of the contract, which was established by both seller and buyer; judging against the absent seller is impermissible. For Abu Yusuf: the buyer claims ownership (yadda'i al-milk li nafsihi), making him a valid opponent for anyone who disputes that.
Notice that the two sides focus on the effect on the absent party, while Abu Yusuf focuses on the buyer's own claim.
4
Apply to the Shuf'ah Analogy
The passage explicitly applies the same difference to a shuf'ah case. Understand why the donee is treated like the buyer: the pre-emptor's claim (shuf'ah) also entails rescinding the gift, which would affect the absent donor (original seller).
There is also a narration from the two sides aligning with Abu Yusuf on shuf'ah, showing some flexibility.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
The text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but in the Hanafi school the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two sides) is dominant and relied upon for fatwa. Abu Yusuf's view is noted but not preferred.
This is important: knowing the dominant view guides practice in courts and fatwa.

Source Text

قال فان كان البائع غائبا فلا خصومة بينهم وبين المشترى معناه اذا انكر الدين وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابویوسف المشترى خصهم ويقضى لهم بدينهم وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا اشترى دارا ووهبها وسلمها وغاب ثم حضر الشفيع فالموهوب له ليس بخصم عندهما خلافا له وعنهما مثل قوله في مسالة الشفعة لابي يوسف انه يدعى الملك لنفسه فيكون خصما لكل من ينازعه ولهما ان الدعوى يتضمن فسخ العقد وقد قام بهما فيكون الفسخ قضاء على الغائب
ترجمہ پھر اگر بائع غائب ہو تو غرماء اور مشتری کے درمیان کوئی خصومت نہ ہوگی۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب مشتری قرضہ کا انکار کرے۔ اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری خصم ہوگا اور غرماء کے لئے ان کے قرضہ کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب ایک مکان خرید کر بہہ کر کے سپرد کرنے کے بعد خود غائب ہو گیا پھر شفیع حاضر ہوا تو موہوب لہ خصم نہ ہوگا طرفین کے نزدیک۔ برخلاف امام ابو یوسف کے اور طرفین سے مسئلہ شفعہ میں ایک روایت قول ابو یوسف کے مثل بھی ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشترکی اپنی ملک کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو وہ خصم ہو گا ہر اس شخص کا جو اس سے جھگڑا کرے ۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دعوی مذکور صبح عقد و متضمن ہے۔ حالانکہ عقد ان دونوں سے قائم ہوا ہے تو فسح کرنا قضاء بر غائب ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله فإن كان البائع الخ - پھر اگر بائع ( آقا ) عبد ماذون کو فروخت کر کے غائب ہو جائے اور مشترکی اس پر قبینہ کو چکا ہو۔ اور اس کے مدیون ہونے کا منکر ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک مشترکی اور قرض خواہوں کے درمیان مخاصمہ نہ ہوگا اور وہ اس کے مد ہونا ہونے کا مقر ہو تو بے شک وہ خصم ہو گا ۔ جیسا کہ مذکور ہو چکا ہے امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری ان کا خصم ( مدعی علیہ ) ہو سکتا ہے اور قرض خواہوں کے لئے ان کے قرضے کا حکم دے دیا جائیگا۔ صاحب ہدایا فرماتے ہیں کہ شفعہ کے مسئلہ میں بھی ایسا ہی اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے کوئی مکان خریدا اور کسی دوسرے کو وہ مکان ہبہ کر کے سپر د کر دیا۔ اس کے بعد خود غائب ہو گیا۔ پھر شفیع حاضر ہوا۔ ( جس کو اس مکان کا شفعہ ملنا ہے ) تو طرفین کے نزدیک موہوب لہ اس کا مدعی علیہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہو سکتا ہے۔ مسئلہ شفعہ میں یہ ایک روایت طرفین سے بھی آئی ہے۔ قوله ابي يوسف ..... الخ - امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری چونکہ اپنی ملکیت کا مدعی ہے اس لئے جو بھی اس سے جھگڑا کرے اس کا مدعی علیہ ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دعوای مذکور فسخ عقد کا متضمن ہے حالانکہ عقد بائع ومشتری ہی کے ذریعہ سے قائم ہوا ہے تو فسح کرنا بائع غائب پر حکم کرنا ہو گا۔ حالانکہ قضاء بر غائب جائز نہیں۔
He said: So if the seller is absent, there is no litigation between them and the buyer, meaning when he denies the debt. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: The buyer is their opponent and judgment is given for their debt. And upon this difference is the case when one buys a house, gifts it, hands it over, then becomes absent; then the pre-emptor comes: the donee is not an opponent according to them, contrary to him. And from them is a narration like his statement in the case of shuf'ah: that Abu Yusuf said he claims ownership for himself, so he is an opponent for anyone who disputes with him. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the claim includes rescission of the contract, and the contract was established by them both, so rescission would be a judgment against the absent party. ... Translation: Then if the seller is absent, there is no litigation between the creditors and the buyer. This means when the buyer denies the debt. And this is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf says the buyer will be an opponent and judgment will be given for their debt. And upon this difference is when one buys a house, gifts it, hands it over, then becomes absent; then the pre-emptor comes: the donee will not be an opponent according to the two sides, contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf. And from the two sides there is also a narration like Abu Yusuf's statement in the case of shuf'ah. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: the buyer claims ownership for himself, so he will be an opponent to anyone who disputes with him. The two sides' proof: the claim includes rescission of the contract, and the contract was established by them both, so rescinding would be a judgment against the absent party. Commentary: ...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when the seller (master) of a ma'dhun slave is absent and the buyer denies the debt, can the creditors sue the buyer? According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two sides), the buyer is not a valid opponent (khasm) because the claim involves rescinding the sale, which would effectively be a judgment against the absent seller, which is not permitted. Abu Yusuf argues that the buyer claims ownership and thus is a proper opponent for anyone disputing that ownership, including creditors. The same dispute applies to a shuf'ah (pre-emption) case: if someone buys a house, gifts it, then goes absent, the donee is not an opponent for the pre-emptor according to the two sides, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. There is also a narration from the two sides supporting Abu Yusuf in the shuf'ah case. The commentary clarifies the reasoning.

Key Terms
خصومہ (khusumah): Litigation or legal dispute between parties in court.
خصم (khasm): An opponent or adversary in a lawsuit, someone who can be sued directly.
شفعہ (shuf'ah): Pre-emption right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property.
فسخ العقد (faskh al-'aqd): Rescission or annulment of a contract.
قضاء على الغائب (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): Judgment against an absent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the buyer not a valid opponent (khasm) when the seller is absent and the buyer denies the debt?
A) Because the buyer does not own the slave
B) Because the claim involves rescinding the contract, which would be a judgment against the absent seller
C) Because the creditors have no right to sue
D) Because the buyer is a minor

Key Takeaway
The buyer is not a valid khasm when the seller is absent because the claim entails rescinding the contract, which would be a judgment against the absent seller—a prohibition in Hanafi law.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on a Claimed Slave's Trade: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Ruling on claimed slave's trade with istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a claimed slave's trade and explain why his transactions are binding based on istihsan, with the distinction between his person (raqabah) and earnings.

Core Idea
A claimed slave's trades are binding; his word on authorization is accepted by istihsan, except for his person.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a person who enters a city, claims to be a slave, and then engages in trade. The Hanafi school rules that his transactions are binding on him, based on the principle of istihsan, which allows departure from strict analogy to facilitate commerce. However, the ruling changes when the master appears, distinguishing between the slave's earnings and his physical person (which belongs solely to the master). Understanding this case sharpens your grasp of how istihsan operates in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is a person claiming to be a slave who then buys and sells. The ruling is that all trade transactions are binding on him (lazim).
The binding is on the slave, not the master initially.
2
Locate the dalil: Istihsan
The author states that if the slave explicitly claims authorization (ma'dhun), his statement is accepted as evidence (daliil) by istihsan. If he does not claim authorization, his trade is still valid because the apparent state (zahir) is that a restricted person acts within his restriction, and acting on the apparent is the basis (asl) in transactions.
The proof is not a textual source but a rational principle: the need to avoid hardship in commercial dealings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The istihsan argument works as follows: requiring proof of authorization from someone who presents himself as trading openly would cause undue hardship. The 'apparent' (zahir) is that such a person is authorized, so we accept his claim or rely on the appearance.
The opposite view (qiyas) would require evidence for the claim of authorization.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The three imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad according to the commentary) follow qiyas: the claim of authorization is a mere claim and should not be accepted without proof. The Hanafi school prefers istihsan.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in usul methods.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih and practical consequence
The Hanafi position facilitates trade and protects the rights of creditors. The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the slave's transactions are initially valid, and if the master confirms authorization, the slave can be sold to pay debts. If the master denies, his word is accepted (original state: slave is restricted), and the slave's trades remain binding on the slave himself but not on the master.
The ruling distinguishes between the slave's person (cannot be sold without master's confirmation) and his earnings (which are his right).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قدم مصرا فقال انا عبد لفلان فاشترى و باع لزمه كل شيء من التجارة لانه ان اخبر بالاذن فالاخبار دليل عليه وان لم يخبر فتصرفه جائز اذ الظاهر ان المحجور على موجب حجره والعمل بالظاهر هو الاصل في المعاملات كيلا يضيق الأمر على الناس الا انه لا يباع حتى يحضر مولاه لانه لا يقبل قوله في الرقبة لانها خالص حق المولى بخلاف الكسب لانه حق العبد على العبد ما بيناه فان حضر وقال هو ماذون بيع في الدين لانه ظهر الدين فى حق المولى وان قال هو محجور فالقول قوله لانه متمسک بالاصل
ترجمہ: ایک شخص نے شہر میں اگر کہا کہ میں فلاں کا غلام ہوں پھر اس نے خرید و فروخت کی تو اس پر لازم ہوگی ہر وہ چیز جواز قسم تجارت ہو اس لئے کہ اگر اس نے اجازت پانے کی خبر دی ہے تو اس کا خبر دینا خود اس پر دلیل ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے یہ خبر نہیں دی تو اس کا تصرف جائز ہے کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ مجو شخص اپنے حجر کے مطابق ہی عمل کریگا۔ اور ظاہر پر عمل کرنا ہی اصل ہے معاملات میں تا کہ لوگوں پر معاملہ تنگ نہ ہو جائے ۔لیکن غلام فروخت نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کا آقا حاضر ہو کیونکہ اپنے رقبہ کی بابت اس کا قول قبول نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس لئے کہ رتبہ تو خالص آقا کا حق ہے بخلاف کمائی کے کہ وہ غلام کا حق ہے۔ پس اگر آقا آ کر کہے کہ وہ ماذون ہے تو قرضہ میں فروخت کر دیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ قرضہ آقا کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہو گیا اور اگر آقا نے کہا کہ وہ مجور ہے تو اس کا قول مقبول ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ وہ اصل سے حجت پکڑ رہا ہے۔ تشریح قوله ومن قدم مصراً ... الخ - ایک شخص نے شہر میں آکر کہا کہ میں فلاں ( مثلا زید ) کا غلام ہوں پھر اس نے خریدو فروخت کی تو جو چیز بھی از قسم تجارت ہو وہ اس پر لازم ہوگی اب یہ مسئلہ دو وجہ پر ہے ایک یہ کہ اس نے اجازت پانے کی خبر دی۔ یعنی اپنا مازون ہونا بیان کیا تو استحسانا اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ خواہ وہ عادل ہو یا غیر عادل اور مقتضائے قیاس یہ ہے کہ اس کی تصدیق نہ کی جائے ۔ چنانچہ ائمہ ثلاثہ اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ کیونکہ یہ اس کی طرف سے ایک دعوی ہے تو بلا حجت تصدیق نہیں ہو سکتی۔
He said: And whoever comes to a city and says, 'I am the slave of so-and-so,' then buys and sells, every thing of trade is binding on him. Because if he informs of authorization, the information is evidence for him; if he does not inform, his transaction is permissible, for the apparent state is that a restricted person acts according to his restriction, and acting on the apparent is the basis in transactions so that affairs are not made difficult for people. But he will not be sold until his master comes, because his statement regarding his person (raqabah) is not accepted, as that is the exclusive right of the master, unlike earnings, which are the slave's right. Then if the master comes and says he is authorized, he is sold for the debt because the debt became apparent regarding the master; if he says he is restricted, his statement is accepted because he holds the original (presumption). Translation: ... Commentary: ...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on a person who comes to a city claiming to be the slave of someone and then engages in trade. All his trade transactions are binding on him. If he explicitly claims authorization (ma'dhun), his statement is accepted as evidence (by istihsan, overriding qiyas which would require proof). Even if he remains silent, his transactions are valid because the default assumption is that a restricted person acts within his restrictions; but here the apparent state is that he is free to trade (since he is openly claiming to be a slave and trading). However, he cannot be sold (to pay debts) until his master appears, because ownership of his person is the master's exclusive right, and his own word is not accepted against that. If the master comes and confirms authorization, the slave can be sold for debt. If the master denies authorization, his word is accepted because the default (original state) is that the slave is not authorized (restricted). The commentary notes that this ruling is based on istihsan; the qiyas (favored by the three imams other than Abu Hanifa) is that his claim of authorization should not be accepted without evidence.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling.
محجور (mahjur): A person legally restricted from conducting financial transactions (e.g., a non-authorized slave).
رقبہ (raqabah): The physical person of a slave, which is the property of the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the master appears and says the slave is not authorized (mahjur)?
A) The slave's previous transactions are voided.
B) The master's statement is accepted and the slave cannot be sold for debt arising from his trades.
C) The slave is immediately set free.
D) The creditors can still sell the slave.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a claimed slave's trade transactions are binding by istihsan to facilitate commerce, but the slave's person cannot be sold without the master's confirmation.
