Profit from Usurped Property: The Dispute Between Imam al-Karkhi and the Mashayikh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on profit from usurped property with indication/payment scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam al-Karkhi's three cases where profit is considered pure, and apply the mashayikh's position that profit is never pure, explaining the tarjih to the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, profit from usurped property is never pure according to the relied-upon position.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding profit when a usurper uses usurped money in a transaction. Imam al-Karkhi carved out three exceptions where the profit remains pure, but the later mashayikh rejected any exception, holding that profit is always impure. Understanding this disagreement is crucial for determining the correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases of Imam al-Karkhi
State the scenarios: (1) indicating specific dirhams but paying from others, (2) paying with those dirhams but indicating others, (3) absolute contract with payment from those dirhams.
The common element is that the specific usurped money is given as payment in some way.
2
Understand the reasoning behind the exception
Imam al-Karkhi argues that indication (isharah) does not effect specification (ta'yin), so impurity (khabath) only realises when payment is actually from the same dirhams.
This is a talil based on the ineffectiveness of isharah for ta'yin.
3
Present the mashayikh's objection
The later mashayikh (our scholars) reject any exception, citing the absolute ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Mabsut that profit is pure without exception.
They interpret 'pure' in those texts as absolute, allowing no qualification.
4
Analyse the tarjih
The mashayikh's view is chosen (mukhtar) because the authoritative texts are unambiguous; the fatwa is on their opinion.
Thus, in practice, profit is never pure.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam al-Karkhi, the usurper may keep the profit in three cases; under the mashayikh, he must always compensate the owner for the profit.
This has direct implications for wealth and charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اما اذا اشار اليها .... الخ ۔ اور اگر ان دراہم کی طرف اشارہ کیا اور ثمن دوسرے دراہم سے ادا کیا ۔ یا شمن میں وہی درہم دیئے اور اشارہ ان کے علاوہ کی طرف کیا یا عقد مطلق رکھا کہ میں نے ہزار کے عوض خریدی اور دام انھیں دراہم سے ادا کئے تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں نفع پاکیزہ رہے گا۔ یہی تفصیلی جواب امام کرخی کا قول ہے ۔ اس لئے کہ جب اشارہ مفید تعیین نہ ہوا تو تحقق خبث کے لئے ضروری ہے انہیں دراہم سے ادائیگی ہو کر تا کید ہو جائے ۔ تمتہ اور ذخیرہ میں ہے کہ فتویٰ امام کرخی کے قول پر ہے۔ قوله وقال مشائخنا ... الخ ۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ ضمان دینے سے پہلے ہو یا اس کے بعد ہو ۔ بہر حال کسی صورت میں نفع پاکیزہ نہیں ہے اور یہی قول مختار ہے کیونکہ جامع صغیر و جامع کبیر اور مبسوط کی کتاب المضاربت میں نفع کے پاکیزہ ہونے کا حکم مطلق ہے۔ یعنی کسی صورت کا استثناء نہیں ہے۔ قوله وان اشتری با لالف ... الخ - اور اگر غاصب نے مخصوبہ ہزار درہم کے عوض ایسی باندی خریدی جو ہزار قیمت کے برابر ہے اور وہ کسی کو ہبہ کردی یا ان کے عوض اناج خریدا۔ اور اس کو کھا لیا تو کچھ صدقہ نہ کرے (بل يرد عليه مثل ما غصب ) یه علم بالاتفاق ہے اس لیے کہ نفع اسی وقت ظاہر ہوتا ہے جب جنس متحد ہو۔ مثلاً اگر باندی یا اناج در اہم کے عوض فروخت کیا جاتا تو ہزار سے جو زائد ہووہ نفع ظاہر ہوتا اور یہاں ایسا نہیں ہوا تو نفع ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔ عین مغصوب فعل غاصب سے متغیر ہوگئی یہاں تک کہ اس کا نام اور بڑی منفعت ختم ہوگئی تو معصومینے کی ملک زائل ہو جائیگی اور غاصب اس کا لک ہوگا اور اس کا ضامن ہوگا انتفاع حلال نہیں یہاں تک کہ اس کا عوض ادا کرے
He said: As for when he indicated to them... etc. And if he indicated to those dirhams and paid the price from other dirhams, or gave those same dirhams as price and indicated to other than them, or made the contract absolute saying 'I bought for a thousand' and paid with those same dirhams, then in these three cases the profit remains pure. This is the detailed answer of Imam al-Karkhi. Because when the indication did not effect specification, for the realization of impurity it is necessary that payment be made with those dirhams to emphasize it. In Tatimma and Dhakhira it is said that the fatwa is on the saying of Imam al-Karkhi. He said: And our mashayikh said: Whether before giving compensation or after, in any case the profit is not pure, and this is the chosen saying, because in al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Mabsut in the book of Mudaraba, the ruling that profit is pure is absolute, i.e., no exception is made for any case. He said: And if he bought with the thousand ... etc. - And if the usurper bought with the usurped thousand dirhams a slave-girl equal in value to a thousand and gave her as a gift, or bought grain with them and ate it, then he should not give any charity (but must return the like of what he usurped). This is agreed upon because profit appears only when the type is one. For example, if the slave-girl or grain were sold for dirhams, then whatever is more than a thousand would be apparent profit, and here that did not happen, so profit does not appear. The usurped property changed by the action of the usurper until its name and great benefit were lost, so the ownership of the usurped-from person is removed, and the usurper becomes its owner and is liable for it, and it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on profit (nafa') when a usurper uses usurped money in a transaction. It begins by quoting Imam al-Karkhi's view that profit remains pure (halal) in three scenarios: (1) when the usurper indicates specific dirhams but pays from other dirhams, (2) when he uses the same dirhams but indicates other than them, or (3) when he makes an absolute contract and pays with those dirhams. The reasoning is that the indication does not effect specification, so impurity (khabath) is only realized when the payment is specifically with those dirhams. According to al-Tatimma and al-Dhakhira, the fatwa is on Imam al-Karkhi's view. However, the later mashayikh (our scholars) hold that in all cases the profit is not pure, whether compensation is given before or after, and this is the chosen (mukhtar) position. They base this on the absolute ruling in the authoritative books (al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Mabsut) that profit is pure without exception. Then the passage discusses a parallel case: if the usurper buys a slave-girl or grain with the thousand dirhams and then gifts or consumes it, he must return the like (mithl) of the usurped property, not charity. This is agreed upon because profit is only apparent when the type is homogeneous (jins muttahid). The passage then concludes with a transitional statement: if the usurped property changes by the usurper's action until its name and great benefit are lost, ownership transfers to the usurper and he must pay its substitute, and he cannot benefit until he does so. This sets up the next section on transformation.

Key Terms
نفع پاکیزہ (nafa' pakizah): Pure profit that is halal to keep without any liability.
اشارہ (isharah): Verbal indication or pointing to specific money in a transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when is profit from usurped property considered pure?
A) When the usurper indicates other money but pays with the usurped money.
B) When the usurper pays with other money but indicates the usurped money.
C) When the contract is absolute and payment is from the usurped money.
D) Never — profit is never pure.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that profit from usurped property is never pure; the usurper must compensate the owner for any gain.

When Usurped Property Changes: The Rule on Profit and Compensation
Agreed ruling on profit and compensation when usurped property is transformed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a usurper transforms usurped property (e.g., by buying and consuming) and determine when profit is apparent.

Core Idea
Profit is only apparent when the exchange involves the same type; transformation of property transfers ownership but requires compensation.

This lesson covers the agreed-upon rule when a usurper uses usurped money to buy goods and then consumes or gifts them. The key principle is that profit is only considered apparent when the exchanged item is of the same type (jins muttahid). Transformation of the property can transfer ownership to the usurper, but he must pay its substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The usurper buys a slave-girl or grain with the usurped money and then gifts or consumes it.
2
Understand the 'agreed upon' ruling
The usurper must return the like (mithl) of the usurped property; he does not need to give charity. This is agreed upon.
This is because the profit is not apparent due to different types.
3
Define 'profit apparent' condition
Profit (nafa') becomes apparent only when the sale or exchange involves items of the same type (jins muttahid). Here, goods are different from dirhams.
If the slave-girl were sold for dirhams, the excess over the usurped amount would be apparent profit.
4
Apply to the case
In the scenario, the usurper did not sell the goods for dirhams, so no apparent profit exists. The profit is not realized.
Thus, no extra charity is required; only the mithl must be returned.
5
Apply the general rule on transformation
If the usurped property changes by the usurper's action until its name and great benefit are lost, ownership transfers to the usurper, and he becomes liable for its substitute.
He cannot benefit from the transformed property without paying compensation.

جنس متحد (jins muttahid): Same type or genus; used to determine when profit is apparent in exchanges.
مثل (mithl): The like or equivalent in value; compensation for usurped property when the original cannot be returned.

Ownership Transfer of Transformed Usurped Property
Rules and disputes when usurped property changes identity and major benefits are lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ownership transfer of usurped property after transformation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
When usurped property's name and major benefits vanish, the usurper becomes owner but must pay compensation.

This passage deals with a fundamental dispute: does the original owner retain ownership when the usurper transforms the property beyond recognition? The Hanafi school answers no—ownership transfers to the usurper upon loss of name and major benefits, but compensation is due. The Shafi'i school and some Hanafi narrations disagree. Let's unpack the legal logic.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the precise ruling: ownership transfers to the usurper when the property's name and most of its benefits are lost due to the usurper's action. The usurper must pay compensation (badal) and cannot benefit without payment.
Examples: wheat ground into flour, iron forged into a sword, a sheep slaughtered and cooked.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the owner's right is not cut off; the property remains with the owner and the craft follows it. A narration from Abu Yusuf also supports this.
Abu Yusuf adds a nuance: if the owner takes the flour, the usurper does not compensate for loss to avoid riba.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof uses qiyas: like wind blowing wheat into another's mill (owner retains ownership), the prohibited act of usurpation cannot transfer ownership. Also, slaughtering a sheep (name remains as 'meat') does not transfer ownership.
The key analogy is that the craft follows the property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that the usurper creates a valuable craft (sana'ah mutaqawwimah), making the owner's right partially destroyed (name and benefits lost) while the usurper's right in the craft is complete. Thus the usurper's right preponderates. Unlike the sheep case, the name changes completely (e.g., wheat to flour).
Qiyas with preponderance (tarjih) is the method.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: For Hanafi, the usurper becomes owner and must pay value; for Shafi'i, the original owner retains ownership and can claim the transformed object without paying for the craft. In Hanafi, if the usurper dies, the property is sold for his debt, and the original owner has priority among creditors.
This affects financial liability and inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يتغير بفعل الغاصب ، قال واذا تغيرت العين المغصوبة بفعل الغاصب حتى زال اسمها واعظم منافعها زال ملك المغصوب منه عنها، وملكها الغاصب وضمنها ولا يحل له الانتفاع بها حتى يودى بدلها كمن غصب شاة وذبحها وشواها او طبخها او حنطة فطبخها او حديدا فاتخذه سيفا او صفرا فعمله آنية وهذا كله عندنا، وقال الشافعي لا ينقطع حق المالك وهو رواية عن ابى يوسف غير انه اذا اختار اخذ الدقيق لا يضمنه النقصان عنده، لانه يؤدى الى الربوا، وعند الشافعي يضمنه وعن ابي يوسف انه يزول ملكه عنه لكنه يباع في دينه وهو احق به من الغرماء بعد موته

ترجمہ فصل ۔ اس چیز میں جو غاصب کے فعل سے متغیر ہو جائے کہ جب متغیر ہو جائے عین مخصو بہ غاصب کے فعل سے یہاں تک کہ اس کا نام اور بڑی منفعت زائل ہو جائے تو اس سے مغصوب منہ کی ملک زائل ہو جائے گی اور غاصب اسکا مالک ہو جائے گا اور اس کا ضامن ہو گا لیکن اس سے انتفاع حلال نہ ہو گا ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کا عوض ادا کر دے۔ جیسے کسی نے بکری غصب کر کے ذبح کی۔ اس کو بھون لیا یا پکا لیا گیہوں غصب کر کے پیس لیا یا لوہا غصب کر کے اس کی تلوار بنالی یا پیتل غصب کر کے برتن بنالیا۔ یہ سب ہمارے نزدیک ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مالک کا حق منقطع نہ ہو گا۔ یہی ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف سے ہے صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر مالک نے آٹالینا اختیار کیا تو اس سے نقصان نہیں لے سکتا۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کیونکہ یہ بیاج تک پہنچا دے گا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لے سکتا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف سے یہ روایت بھی ہے کہ اس سے مالک کی ملک زائل ہو جائے گی اور اس کے قرضہ میں اسکو فر رخت کر دیا جائے گا اور غاصب کے مرنے کے بعد دیگر قرض خواہوں کی بہ نسبت مالک اس کا زیادہ حق دار ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله واذا تغيرت الخ - غاصب نے کوئی چیز غصب کی اور اس کو اس طرح متغیر کر دیا کہ اس کا نام اور اس کے اکثر مقاصد زائل ہو گئے ۔ مثلاً مغصوب بکری تھی اس کو ذبح کر کے بھون لیا یا پکا لیا ۔ یا گیہوں تھے اس کو پیس لیا یا کھیت میں بیج ڈال دیا یا لو ہا تھا اس کی تلوار بنالی یا پیلی تھی اس کا برتن بنالیا یا اس میں کوئی ایسا تصرف کیا جس کی وجہ سے وہ غاصب کی ملک کے ساتھ اس طرح مخلوط ہو گئی کہ اس کا جدا ہونا ممتنع ہو گیا ۔ مثلاً مغصوب ساگون لکڑی کا لٹھا تھا غاصب نے اس پر عمارت بنالی تو ان سب صورتوں میں ہمارے نزدیک غاصب ان کا مالک ہو جائے گا ۔ امام شافعی کے ہاں ان صورتوں میں اصل مالک کا حق منقطع نہیں ہوتا۔ یہ ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف سے بھی ہے اور یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ اگر مالک آنالینا اختیار کرے تو غاصب سے نقصان نہیں لے سکتا کیونکہ اس سے بیاج لازم آئے گا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نقصان لے سکتا ہے۔ نیز امام ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ بھی ہے کہ اس سے مالک کی چیز زائل ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اگر غاصب مر جائے تو اصل مالک کے قرضہ میں وہ چیز فروخت کر دی جائے گی ۔ مثلا آنا فروخت کر کے اس کے مثل گیہوں خرید کر مالک کو دئے جائیں گے اور دیگر قرض خواہوں کی بہ نسبت مالک اس کا زیادہ حقدار ہوگا۔

امام شافعی و احناف کی دلیل
للشافعي ان العين باق فيبقى على ملكه وتتبعه الصنعة، كما اذا هبت الريح فى الحنطة والقتها في طاحونة الغير فطحنت ولا معتبر بفعله لانه محظور فلا يصلح سببا للملك على ما عرف قصار كما اذا انعدم الفعل اصلا وصار كما اذا ذبح الشاة المغصوبة وسلخها واربها ولنا انه احدث صنعة متقومة فيصير حق المالك هالكا من وجه الا ترى انه تبدل الاسم وفات معظم المقاصد وحقه في الصنعة قائم من كل وجه، فيترجح على الاصل الذي هو فائت من وجه ولا نجعله سببا للملك من حيث انه محظور بل من حيث انه احداث الصنعة بخلاف الشاة، لان اسمها باق بعد الذبح والسلخ ، وهذا الوجه يشمل الفصول المذكورة ويتفرع عليه غيرها فاحفظه
Chapter: What changes by the action of the usurper. He said: When the usurped property changes by the action of the usurper until its name and most of its benefits are lost, the ownership of the usurped-from person is removed from it, and the usurper owns it and is liable for it, and it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute. Like one who usurps a sheep and slaughters it, roasts it, or cooks it; or wheat and cooks it; or iron and makes it into a sword; or brass and makes it into a vessel. All this is according to us (Hanafis). Al-Shafi'i said: the right of the owner is not cut off. And there is a narration from Abu Yusuf, except that if the owner chooses to take the flour, the usurper does not compensate the loss according to him, because it leads to riba; but according to al-Shafi'i, he does compensate. And from Abu Yusuf there is also a narration that his (the owner's) ownership is removed, but it is sold for his (the usurper's) debt, and he (the owner) has more right to it than other creditors after his death.

Translation: Chapter: In that which changes by the action of the usurper. When the usurped property changes by the action of the usurper until its name and great benefit are lost, the ownership of the usurped-from person is removed, and the usurper becomes its owner and is liable for it, but it is not permissible for him to benefit from it until he pays its substitute. Like someone who usurps a sheep and slaughters it, roasts it, or cooks it; or usurps wheat and grinds it; or iron and makes it into a sword; or brass and makes it into a vessel. All this is according to us (Hanafis). Imam al-Shafi'i says: the owner's right is not cut off. This is also a narration from Abu Yusuf. Only that if the owner chooses to take the flour, he cannot claim the loss from the usurper according to him, because it would lead to riba; and according to al-Shafi'i, he can claim the loss. And from Abu Yusuf there is also a narration that the owner's ownership is removed, and it is sold for his debt, and after the death of the usurper, the owner has more right to it than other creditors.

Elaboration of his statement 'and when it changes...' - The usurper usurped something and changed it in such a way that its name and most of its purposes were lost. For example, the usurped was a sheep, he slaughtered it and roasted or cooked it; or it was wheat, he ground it or sowed it in the field; or it was iron, he made it into a sword; or it was brass, he made it into a vessel; or he performed such an act that it mixed with the usurper's property in such a way that separation is impossible. For example, the usurped was a teak log, and the usurper built a structure on it. In all these cases, according to us, the usurper becomes the owner of them. According to al-Shafi'i, the original owner's right is not cut off. This is also a narration from Abu Yusuf, and it is the saying of Imam Ahmad. Only difference is that if the owner chooses to take the flour, he cannot claim the loss from the usurper because it would necessitate riba; and according to al-Shafi'i, he can claim the loss. Also, from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that the owner's property is removed. But if the usurper dies, that property is sold for the debt of the original owner. For example, the flour is sold and wheat similar to it is bought and given to the owner, and the owner has more right to it than other creditors.

The proof of al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis:
For al-Shafi'i: The property remains, so it remains in his ownership, and the craft follows it, as when the wind blows the wheat and throws it into another's mill and it is ground; no consideration is given to his action because it is prohibited, so it cannot be a cause for ownership, as if the action did not exist at all, and it is like when one slaughters the usurped sheep, skins it, and cuts it into pieces.
For us (Hanafis): He created a valuable craft (sana'ah mutaqawwimah), so the owner's right becomes destroyed from one aspect. Do you not see that the name changed and most purposes were lost? And his right in the craft is established from all aspects, so it is preponderant over the original which is lost from one aspect. And we do not make it a cause for ownership because it is prohibited, but because of the creation of the craft. Unlike the sheep, because its name remains after slaughter and skinning. And this aspect encompasses the mentioned chapters, and other rulings branch from it. So preserve it.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the transformation (taghayyur) of usurped property by the usurper's action, along with the Shafi'i position and two narrations from Abu Yusuf. The chapter heading (fasl) opens the discussion. The Hanafi position: when the usurped property changes to the extent that its name (ism) and most of its benefits (muqasid) are lost, the ownership of the original owner (maghsud minhu) is removed and the usurper becomes the owner, but he must pay its substitute (badal) and cannot benefit from it until he does. Examples include slaughtering and cooking a sheep, grinding wheat, making iron into a sword, or brass into a vessel. This is the *zahir al-riwayah* position. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, asserting that the owner's right (haq al-malik) is not cut off; the property remains with the owner and the craft follows it. This is also a narration from Abu Yusuf. However, a key difference: if the owner chooses to take the flour (in case of wheat), Abu Yusuf says the usurper does not compensate the loss (naqsan) because it would lead to riba; Shafi'i says he does compensate. Another narration from Abu Yusuf states that the usurper's ownership is removed, but the property is sold for the usurper's debt, and after his death, the original owner has priority over other creditors. The commentary (tashrih) elaborates with more examples, including mixing that prevents separation (e.g., building on a teak log). The discussion concludes with the legal proofs (dalil) for both schools. The Shafi'i proof uses an analogy: like wind blowing wheat into another's mill, the owner's right persists; the act is prohibited so it cannot transfer ownership, similar to slaughtering and cutting up a sheep (where name remains). The Hanafi proof: the usurper creates a valuable craft (sana'ah mutaqawwimah), so the owner's right in the original is destroyed from one aspect (name and benefits lost) while the craft is entirely created by the usurper; thus the usurper's right prevails. Unlike the sheep, where the name 'meat' remains after slaughter. This principle covers all mentioned cases and branches into others.

Key Terms
عين مغصوبة (al-'ayn al-maghsubah): The specific physical property that was usurped, as opposed to its value or legal liability.
صنعة متقومة (sana'ah mutaqawwimah): A valuable craft or manufactured item that has economic worth, created by the usurper's labor on the usurped property.
زوال الاسم وأعظم المنافع (zawal al-ism wa a'zam al-manafi'): Loss of the original name (e.g., wheat becomes flour) and the most significant benefits of the property, indicating a fundamental change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following transfers ownership of usurped property to the usurper?
A) Slaughtering and cutting a sheep into meat and bones.
B) Grinding wheat into flour.
C) Moving the property to a different location.
D) Using the property without damaging it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when usurped property undergoes a fundamental change losing its name and primary benefits, the usurper becomes owner but must pay the original value.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
The Usurper's Ownership and the Prohibition of Benefit Before Compensation
Expansion on the ruling that the usurper owns but cannot use until compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a usurper's right to benefit from usurped property and explain the hadith proof that establishes the prohibition using istihsan.

Core Idea
A usurper owns the property but cannot use it until compensating the owner — ownership does not imply unrestricted use.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Hanafi fiqh on ghasb (usurpation). The usurper acquires ownership of the misappropriated item, yet the school holds that he is prohibited from benefiting from it until he compensates the original owner. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) supported by a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). We will unpack the proof and understand why ownership alone does not grant permission to use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its elements
State the three parts: (1) the usurper becomes owner, (2) benefiting before compensation is haram, (3) after compensation it becomes permissible. Note that sale and gift are valid despite the prohibition.
The ruling is in the passage: 'غاصب گو مغصوب کا مالک ہو جائے گا لیکن ادائیگی ضمان سے قبل اس کے لئے انتفاع حلال نہ ہو گا'
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith of the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's permission. The Prophet ordered it to be given to captives.
The hadith is cited as the basis of istihsan and is presented with its chain.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
Analyze how the hadith proves the prohibition: the command 'feed it to the captives' indicates that the usurper himself cannot benefit, and the original owner's ownership is removed. The imperative implies prohibition for personal use until compensation.
The commentator explains: 'افاد الامر بالتصدق زوال ملك المالك وحرمة الانتفاع للغاصب قبل الارضاء'.
4
Note the role of istihsan
Understand that the apparent qiyas would permit benefit because ownership is absolute. However, istihsan overrides qiyas to prevent opening the door to usurpation (sadd al-dhara'i').
The text says: 'وفي اباحة الانتفاع فتح باب الغصب فيحرم قبل الارضاء حسما لمادة الفساد'.
5
Recognize the authority of the proof
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is relied upon in the madhhab. The commentator defends its authenticity against criticism by Abu Dawud.
The chain is through Asim ibn Kulayb, who is considered trustworthy by Ibn Sa'd and Ibn Hibban.

وجه استحسان
وجه الاستحسان قوله عليه السلام فى الشاة المذبوحة المصلية بغير رضاء صاحبها اطعموها الأسارى افاد الامر بالتصدق زوال ملك المالك وحرمة الانتفاع للغاصب قبل الارضاء ولان في اباحة الانتفاع فتح باب الغصب فيحرم قبل الارضاء حسما لمادة الفساد، ونفاذ بيعه وهبته مع الحرمة لقيام الملک کما فی الملک الفاسد، واذا ادى البدل يباح له لان حق المالك صار موفى بالبدل فحصلت مبدالة بالتراضى و ، وكذا اذا ابراد لسقوط حقه به وكذا اذا ادى بالقضاء او ضمنه الحاكم او ضمنه المالك لوجود الرضاء منه، لانه لا يقضى الا بطلبه وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا غصب حنطة فزرعها او نواة فغرسها غير ان عند ابي يوسف يباح الانتفاع فيهما قبل اداء الضمان لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه بخلاف ما تقدم لقيام العين فيه من وجه وفي الحنطة يزرعها لا يتصدق بالفـ لفضل ـل عنده خلافا لهـ واصله ما تقدم
توضیح اللغة .. مصلیہ بھوئی ہوئی ، اساری جمع اسیر بمعنی قیدی ، ارضاء خوش کرنا، حسماً (ض) جڑ سے کاٹنا۔ موفی پورا کیا ہوا، نواة کھلی ، غرسها (ض) غرساً پودہ لگانا ۔

تشريح ... قوله وجه الاستحسان ... الخ - وجہ استحسان ایک صحابی کی حدیث ہے جس کی تخریج امام ابوداؤد، امام احمد اور دارقطنی نے کی ہے
قال خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في جنازة فرايت رسول الله وهو على القبر يوصى الحافر اوسع من قبل رجلبه : اوسع من قبل راسه : فلما رجع استقبله داعى امرأة فجاء وجنى بالطعام فوضع يده ثم وضع القوم فاكلوا فنظر آباؤنا رسول الله يلوك لقمة فى فيه ثم قال: اني اجد لحم شاة اخذت بغیر اذن اهلها، فارسلت المرأة يا رسول الله اني ارسلت الى البقيع ليشترى لى شاة فلم اجد فارسلت الى جـار لـي قد اشترى شاة ان ارسل الى بثمنها فلم يوجد فارسلت الى امرأته فارسلت بها الى فقال عليه السلام اطعميه الاساری
ایک انصاری صحابی فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ ایک جنازہ میں نکلے تو میں نے دیکھا کہ قبر پر کھڑے ہوئے گورکن کو تعلیم دے رہے ہیں۔ پائینتی کی طرف ذرا اور کھول۔ سر کی طرف اور کشادہ کر ، جب آپ لوٹے تو ایک عورت کی طرف بلانے والا آیا آپ وہاں تشریف لائے کھانا سامنے آیا پس پہلے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پھر اور لوگوں نے ہاتھ بڑھایا اور کھانا شروع کیا ، ہمارے بزرگوں نے آپ کو دیکھا کہ آپ ایک ہی لقمہ چہارے ہیں (اور وہ حلق سے نیچے نہیں اترتا ) پھر آپ نے فرمایا۔ ایسا معلوم ہوتا ہے یہ ایسی بکری کا گوشت ہے جو اس کے مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر لی گئی ہے اس عورت نے کہلا بھیجا، یارسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم میں نے بقیع میں ایک بکری خریدنے کے لئے بھیجا تو بکری نہیں ملی ۔ پس میں نے اپنے ہمسایہ کے پاس کہلا بھیجا کہ جو بکری تم نے خریدی ہے وہ اس قیمت پر مجھے دے دو۔ تو ہمسایہ بھی گھر میں نہیں تھا۔ تو میں نے اس عورت کو کہلا بھیجا، اس نے بکری میرے پاس بھیج دی۔ پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا یہ گوشت قیدیوں کو کھلا دے۔ سوال... امام ابوداؤ نے اس حدیث کی اسناد میں جرح کی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عاصم بـن كـلـيـب عن ابيه عن جده لیس بشئی
جواب ... موصوف کا یہ قول کچھ مصر نہیں۔ کیونکہ عاصم کی یہ روایت عن ابیہ عن جدہ نہیں بلکہ عن ابيه عن رجل من الانصار ہے پھر عاصم بن کلیب ثقہ راوی ہے اور اس کا باپ کلیب بن شہاب بن الجون انجیر کی بھی ثقہ ہے۔ ابن سعد نے کہا ہے کہ نقةً ورأيتهم يستحسنون حديثه ويحتجون به ابن حبان نے بھی اس کو ثقات میں بھی ذکر کیا ہے اور امام بخاری نے جز ما رفع الیدین میں اس سے روایت کی ہے اس حدیث کو دارقطنی نے بھی روایت کیا ہے اس کی اسناد میں حمید بن الربیع الخزاز کی بابت ابن الجوزی نے اتحقیق میں
Book of Ghasp. ... For the establishment of absolute ownership is proven. Do you not see that if he gifts or sells it, it is permissible? Explanation of His statement 'And it is not permissible for him...' etc. - Then according to us, the usurper becomes owner of the usurped property, but before payment of compensation, benefiting from it is not lawful for him. According to Hasan ibn Ziyad and Imam Zufar, benefiting is lawful, and this is also required by analogy, and from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration by Faqih Abu Layth to the same effect. The reason is that absolute ownership is established for the usurper, so benefiting becomes permissible. Do you not see that if the usurper gifts or sells it, it is permissible because he became its owner due to a lawful reason? So this is like property possessed through a defective sale, whose sale is valid. Benefit: It is narrated from the fatwas of the people of Samarqand at the end of the book of Ghasp in Khulasat al-Fatawa that a person usurped food, chewed it, consumed it, and it passed out. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he swallowed it lawfully, and the condition of purity is bodily obligation according to him, and according to the Two Companions (Sahibayn), it is payment of replacement, and the fatwa is upon the saying of the Two Companions. The basis of istihsan: The basis of istihsan is his statement, peace be upon him, regarding the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's consent: 'Feed it to the captives.' This command to give charity indicated the removal of the owner's ownership and the prohibition of benefit for the usurper before obtaining satisfaction. And because permitting benefit would open the door to usurpation, so it is prohibited before satisfaction to cut off the root of corruption. And the validity of his sale and gift despite the prohibition is due to the existence of ownership, as in defective ownership. And when he pays the replacement, it becomes permissible for him, because the owner's right is fulfilled by the replacement, so a mutual exchange occurs by consent. Similarly, if the owner releases him (by ibra'), because his right falls; similarly, if he pays by judicial order, or the judge or the owner makes him liable for compensation, due to the existence of satisfaction from the owner, because the judge only orders at his request. And this difference applies when he usurps wheat and plants it, or a date pit and plants it, except that according to Abu Yusuf, benefiting from both is permissible before payment of compensation due to complete consumption from every aspect, unlike what preceded because the substance remains from an aspect. And regarding the wheat he plants, he does not give the surplus in charity according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to him, and its basis is what preceded. Language clarification: 'Musalya' means roasted, 'Asara' is plural of 'Asir' meaning captive, 'Irda' means pleasing, 'Hasman' means cutting off, 'Muwaffa' means fulfilled, 'Nawa' means date pit, 'Gharasaha' means to plant. Translation: The basis of istihsan is the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's consent: 'Feed it to the captives.' The command to give charity indicated the removal of the owner's ownership and the prohibition of benefit for the usurper before satisfaction. And because permitting benefit would open the door to usurpation, so benefit was prohibited before satisfaction to cut off the root of corruption. And despite the prohibition, the validity of his sale and gift is due to the existence of ownership, as in defective ownership. And when the usurper pays the compensation, it becomes permissible for him, because by paying the replacement, the owner's right is fulfilled. So a mutual exchange is achieved by consent. Similarly, if the owner releases him by ibra' due to the fall of his right; similarly, if he pays by judicial decree or the judge or the owner makes him liable for compensation, due to the existence of the owner's satisfaction, because the judge only orders at his request. And this same difference applies when he usurps wheat and plants it, or a pit and plants it. The only thing is that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, in both cases benefiting is permissible before payment of compensation due to complete consumption from every aspect, unlike what preceded because the substance remains from an aspect. And in the case of planted wheat, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he will not give the surplus in charity, contrary to the Two Companions, and its basis is what has passed. Explanation: 'The basis of istihsan' etc. The basis of istihsan is a hadith from a Companion, produced by Imam Abu Dawud, Imam Ahmad, and Darqutni. He said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, to a funeral. I saw the Messenger of Allah standing at the grave instructing the digger: 'Make it wider from the direction of his feet; make it wider from the direction of his head.' When he returned, he was met by a woman's caller. He came and food was brought. He placed his hand, then the people placed theirs and ate. Our elders saw the Messenger of Allah chewing a morsel in his mouth. Then he said: 'I find the meat of a sheep that was taken without the permission of its owners.' The woman sent word: 'O Messenger of Allah, I sent to al-Baqi' to buy me a sheep but could not find one. Then I sent to my neighbor who had bought a sheep, asking him to send it at its price, but he was not found. So I sent to his wife, and she sent it to me.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'Feed it to the captives.' An Ansari Companion says: We went out with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to a funeral. I saw him standing at the grave instructing the digger to make it wider from the feet side and wider from the head side. When he returned, a woman's caller came. He went there. Food was presented. He first, then the people, extended their hands and began eating. Our elders saw that he was chewing a single morsel and it would not go down his throat. Then he said: 'It seems this is the meat of a sheep that was taken without its owner's permission.' The woman sent word: 'O Messenger of Allah, I sent to al-Baqi' to buy a sheep but did not find one. So I sent to my neighbor who had bought a sheep, asking him to give it to me at that price, but the neighbor was not at home. So I sent to his wife, and she sent the sheep to me.' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Feed this meat to the captives.' Question: Imam Abu Dawud criticized the chain of this hadith. He says: 'Asim ibn Kulayb, from his father, from his grandfather, is nothing.' Answer: This statement of his is not substantiated, because this narration of Asim is not 'from his father from his grandfather' but rather 'from his father from a man of the Ansar.' Moreover, Asim ibn Kulayb is a trustworthy narrator, and his father Kulayb ibn Shihab ibn al-Jawn is also trustworthy. Ibn Sa'd said: 'He is trustworthy, and I saw that they considered his hadith good and used it as evidence.' Ibn Hibban also mentioned him among the trustworthy. Imam al-Bukhari narrated from him in Juz' Raf' al-Yadayn. This hadith was also narrated by Darqutni. Regarding its chain, concerning Humayd ibn al-Rabi' al-Khazzaz, Ibn al-Jawzi said in al-Tahqiq...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a commentary (sharh) on the Hidaya's ruling that a usurper (ghasib) becomes the owner of the usurped property but cannot benefit from it until he pays compensation (daman). The commentary first presents the general rule: the usurper acquires ownership (milk) of the misappropriated item, yet benefiting from it is prohibited (haram) until he compensates the original owner. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon view of the madhhab. It then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Hasan ibn Ziyad and Imam Zufar hold that benefiting is permissible even before compensation, and this is also the apparent requirement of qiyas (analogy). However, the madhhab adopts istihsan (juristic preference) to prevent opening the door to usurpation. The commentary further clarifies that despite the prohibition of use, the usurper's sale or gift of the item is valid because he has ownership, analogous to property acquired through a defective sale (bay' fasid). A practical fatwa from Samarqand is cited: if a person usurps food and consumes it completely, according to Abu Hanifa he swallows it lawfully (as compensation is owed bodily), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) require monetary compensation, and the fatwa is on their view. The second part explains the istihsan reasoning, primarily based on the hadith of the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's permission. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that it be given to captives, which demonstrates that (1) the original owner's ownership is removed upon usurpation, and (2) the usurper cannot benefit before satisfying the owner (i.e., obtaining consent or paying compensation). The hadith is then presented in detail with its narration and chain criticism. The commentator defends the hadith's authenticity against Imam Abu Dawud's criticism, stating that the chain is sound through Asim ibn Kulayb from his father from a man of the Ansar, and that Asim and his father are trustworthy narrators. The discussion ends mid-sentence on page 348 regarding Humayd ibn al-Rabi' al-Khazzaz.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): The unlawful seizure of someone else's property without their consent.
ضمان (daman): Compensation or liability for the value or equivalent of the usurped property.
انتفاع (intifa'): Benefiting from a property, such as using or consuming it.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides an analogy due to a stronger evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a usurper benefiting from the usurped property before compensation?
A) It is permissible because he owns the property.
B) It is prohibited (haram).
C) It is permissible only if the property is consumed completely.
D) It is permissible if the usurper intends to pay later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits a usurper from benefiting before compensation, using istihsan based on the hadith of the sheep.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Usurper's Benefit and Practical Applications
Intra-Hanafi dispute on usurper's benefit and practical applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and others regarding a usurper's benefit before compensation, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to specific cases like planting or consuming food.

Core Idea
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference on whether a usurper may benefit before compensation; the fatwa favors the prohibition, but with exceptions for complete consumption.

Building on the basic ruling, this lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) on the permissibility of benefit before compensation. We explore the views of Hasan ibn Ziyad, Imam Zufar, and the Sahibayn, and the practical differences that arise in cases of complete consumption, planting, and sale. Understanding these nuances is crucial for applying the correct ruling in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the points of ikhtilaf
Note the different opinions: Abu Hanifa prohibits benefit before compensation; Hasan ibn Ziyad and Imam Zufar permit it based on absolute ownership. Also, Abu Yusuf allows benefit in cases of complete consumption (istihlak) like planting wheat or seeds.
The passage mentions: 'حسن بن زیاد اور امام زفر کے نزدیک انتفاع حلال ہے' and later 'عند ابي يوسف يباح الانتفاع فيهما قبل اداء الضمان'.
2
Examine the proof for each side
The opposing view uses qiyas: since ownership is absolute, benefit should be allowed. The Hanafi view uses istihsan from the hadith to prohibit benefit to prevent corruption.
Qiyas: 'مقتضاء قیاس بھی یہی ہے'. Istihsan: based on the hadith and sadd al-dhara'i'.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: can the usurper eat, wear, or use the property before compensating? According to the mufta bihi, no; according to the opposing view, yes. In the case of food consumption, the fatwa follows the Sahibayn (require compensation payment) rather than Abu Hanifa (bodily obligation).
The Samarqand fatwa: 'فتوی صاحبین کے قول پر ہے' regarding food consumption.
4
Apply to specific cases
Work through the examples: usurping wheat and planting it, or a date pit and planting it. According to Abu Yusuf, benefit is permissible before compensation due to complete consumption. Abu Hanifa disagrees and rules that surplus from planted wheat should not be given in charity (contrary to Sahibayn).
The passage: 'وفي الحنطة يزرعها لا يتصدق بالفضل عنده خلافا له'.
5
Recognize the fatwa hierarchy
Note the mufta bihi: prohibition before compensation is the relied-upon view, but for food consumption, the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view (monetary compensation). This shows that later Hanafi masters sometimes choose the view that prevents harm most effectively.
The commentator supports the prohibition but defers to the Sahibayn on food consumption.

وجه استحسان
وجه الاستحسان قوله عليه السلام فى الشاة المذبوحة المصلية بغير رضاء صاحبها اطعموها الأسارى افاد الامر بالتصدق زوال ملك المالك وحرمة الانتفاع للغاصب قبل الارضاء ولان في اباحة الانتفاع فتح باب الغصب فيحرم قبل الارضاء حسما لمادة الفساد، ونفاذ بيعه وهبته مع الحرمة لقيام الملک کما فی الملک الفاسد، واذا ادى البدل يباح له لان حق المالك صار موفى بالبدل فحصلت مبدالة بالتراضى و ، وكذا اذا ابراد لسقوط حقه به وكذا اذا ادى بالقضاء او ضمنه الحاكم او ضمنه المالك لوجود الرضاء منه، لانه لا يقضى الا بطلبه وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا غصب حنطة فزرعها او نواة فغرسها غير ان عند ابي يوسف يباح الانتفاع فيهما قبل اداء الضمان لوجود الاستهلاك من كل وجه بخلاف ما تقدم لقيام العين فيه من وجه وفي الحنطة يزرعها لا يتصدق بالفـ لفضل ـل عنده خلافا لهـ واصله ما تقدم

قال خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في جنازة فرايت رسول الله وهو على القبر يوصى الحافر اوسع من قبل رجلبه : اوسع من قبل راسه : فلما رجع استقبله داعى امرأة فجاء وجنى بالطعام فوضع يده ثم وضع القوم فاكلوا فنظر آباؤنا رسول الله يلوك لقمة فى فيه ثم قال: اني اجد لحم شاة اخذت بغیر اذن اهلها، فارسلت المرأة يا رسول الله اني ارسلت الى البقيع ليشترى لى شاة فلم اجد فارسلت الى جـار لـي قد اشترى شاة ان ارسل الى بثمنها فلم يوجد فارسلت الى امرأته فارسلت بها الى فقال عليه السلام اطعميه الاساری

جواب ... موصوف کا یہ قول کچھ مصر نہیں۔ کیونکہ عاصم کی یہ روایت عن ابیہ عن جدہ نہیں بلکہ عن ابيه عن رجل من الانصار ہے پھر عاصم بن کلیب ثقہ راوی ہے اور اس کا باپ کلیب بن شہاب بن الجون انجیر کی بھی ثقہ ہے۔ ابن سعد نے کہا ہے کہ نقةً ورأيتهم يستحسنون حديثه ويحتجون به ابن حبان نے بھی اس کو ثقات میں بھی ذکر کیا ہے اور امام بخاری نے جز ما رفع الیدین میں اس سے روایت کی ہے اس حدیث کو دارقطنی نے بھی روایت کیا ہے اس کی اسناد میں حمید بن الربیع الخزاز کی بابت ابن الجوزی نے اتحقیق میں
Book of Ghasp. ... For the establishment of absolute ownership is proven. Do you not see that if he gifts or sells it, it is permissible? Explanation of His statement 'And it is not permissible for him...' etc. - Then according to us, the usurper becomes owner of the usurped property, but before payment of compensation, benefiting from it is not lawful for him. According to Hasan ibn Ziyad and Imam Zufar, benefiting is lawful, and this is also required by analogy, and from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration by Faqih Abu Layth to the same effect. The reason is that absolute ownership is established for the usurper, so benefiting becomes permissible. Do you not see that if the usurper gifts or sells it, it is permissible because he became its owner due to a lawful reason? So this is like property possessed through a defective sale, whose sale is valid. Benefit: It is narrated from the fatwas of the people of Samarqand at the end of the book of Ghasp in Khulasat al-Fatawa that a person usurped food, chewed it, consumed it, and it passed out. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he swallowed it lawfully, and the condition of purity is bodily obligation according to him, and according to the Two Companions (Sahibayn), it is payment of replacement, and the fatwa is upon the saying of the Two Companions. The basis of istihsan: The basis of istihsan is his statement, peace be upon him, regarding the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's consent: 'Feed it to the captives.' This command to give charity indicated the removal of the owner's ownership and the prohibition of benefit for the usurper before obtaining satisfaction. And because permitting benefit would open the door to usurpation, so it is prohibited before satisfaction to cut off the root of corruption. And the validity of his sale and gift despite the prohibition is due to the existence of ownership, as in defective ownership. And when he pays the replacement, it becomes permissible for him, because the owner's right is fulfilled by the replacement, so a mutual exchange occurs by consent. Similarly, if the owner releases him (by ibra'), because his right falls; similarly, if he pays by judicial order, or the judge or the owner makes him liable for compensation, due to the existence of satisfaction from the owner, because the judge only orders at his request. And this difference applies when he usurps wheat and plants it, or a date pit and plants it, except that according to Abu Yusuf, benefiting from both is permissible before payment of compensation due to complete consumption from every aspect, unlike what preceded because the substance remains from an aspect. And regarding the wheat he plants, he does not give the surplus in charity according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to him, and its basis is what preceded. Language clarification: 'Musalya' means roasted, 'Asara' is plural of 'Asir' meaning captive, 'Irda' means pleasing, 'Hasman' means cutting off, 'Muwaffa' means fulfilled, 'Nawa' means date pit, 'Gharasaha' means to plant. Translation: The basis of istihsan is the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's consent: 'Feed it to the captives.' The command to give charity indicated the removal of the owner's ownership and the prohibition of benefit for the usurper before satisfaction. And because permitting benefit would open the door to usurpation, so benefit was prohibited before satisfaction to cut off the root of corruption. And despite the prohibition, the validity of his sale and gift is due to the existence of ownership, as in defective ownership. And when the usurper pays the compensation, it becomes permissible for him, because by paying the replacement, the owner's right is fulfilled. So a mutual exchange is achieved by consent. Similarly, if the owner releases him by ibra' due to the fall of his right; similarly, if he pays by judicial decree or the judge or the owner makes him liable for compensation, due to the existence of the owner's satisfaction, because the judge only orders at his request. And this same difference applies when he usurps wheat and plants it, or a pit and plants it. The only thing is that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, in both cases benefiting is permissible before payment of compensation due to complete consumption from every aspect, unlike what preceded because the substance remains from an aspect. And in the case of planted wheat, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he will not give the surplus in charity, contrary to the Two Companions, and its basis is what has passed. Explanation: 'The basis of istihsan' etc. The basis of istihsan is a hadith from a Companion, produced by Imam Abu Dawud, Imam Ahmad, and Darqutni. He said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, to a funeral. I saw the Messenger of Allah standing at the grave instructing the digger: 'Make it wider from the direction of his feet; make it wider from the direction of his head.' When he returned, he was met by a woman's caller. He came and food was brought. He placed his hand, then the people placed theirs and ate. Our elders saw the Messenger of Allah chewing a morsel in his mouth. Then he said: 'I find the meat of a sheep that was taken without the permission of its owners.' The woman sent word: 'O Messenger of Allah, I sent to al-Baqi' to buy me a sheep but could not find one. Then I sent to my neighbor who had bought a sheep, asking him to send it at its price, but he was not found. So I sent to his wife, and she sent it to me.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'Feed it to the captives.' An Ansari Companion says: We went out with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to a funeral. I saw him standing at the grave instructing the digger to make it wider from the feet side and wider from the head side. When he returned, a woman's caller came. He went there. Food was presented. He first, then the people, extended their hands and began eating. Our elders saw that he was chewing a single morsel and it would not go down his throat. Then he said: 'It seems this is the meat of a sheep that was taken without its owner's permission.' The woman sent word: 'O Messenger of Allah, I sent to al-Baqi' to buy a sheep but did not find one. So I sent to my neighbor who had bought a sheep, asking him to give it to me at that price, but the neighbor was not at home. So I sent to his wife, and she sent the sheep to me.' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Feed this meat to the captives.' Question: Imam Abu Dawud criticized the chain of this hadith. He says: 'Asim ibn Kulayb, from his father, from his grandfather, is nothing.' Answer: This statement of his is not substantiated, because this narration of Asim is not 'from his father from his grandfather' but rather 'from his father from a man of the Ansar.' Moreover, Asim ibn Kulayb is a trustworthy narrator, and his father Kulayb ibn Shihab ibn al-Jawn is also trustworthy. Ibn Sa'd said: 'He is trustworthy, and I saw that they considered his hadith good and used it as evidence.' Ibn Hibban also mentioned him among the trustworthy. Imam al-Bukhari narrated from him in Juz' Raf' al-Yadayn. This hadith was also narrated by Darqutni. Regarding its chain, concerning Humayd ibn al-Rabi' al-Khazzaz, Ibn al-Jawzi said in al-Tahqiq...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a commentary (sharh) on the Hidaya's ruling that a usurper (ghasib) becomes the owner of the usurped property but cannot benefit from it until he pays compensation (daman). The commentary first presents the general rule: the usurper acquires ownership (milk) of the misappropriated item, yet benefiting from it is prohibited (haram) until he compensates the original owner. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon view of the madhhab. It then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Hasan ibn Ziyad and Imam Zufar hold that benefiting is permissible even before compensation, and this is also the apparent requirement of qiyas (analogy). However, the madhhab adopts istihsan (juristic preference) to prevent opening the door to usurpation. The commentary further clarifies that despite the prohibition of use, the usurper's sale or gift of the item is valid because he has ownership, analogous to property acquired through a defective sale (bay' fasid). A practical fatwa from Samarqand is cited: if a person usurps food and consumes it completely, according to Abu Hanifa he swallows it lawfully (as compensation is owed bodily), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) require monetary compensation, and the fatwa is on their view. The second part explains the istihsan reasoning, primarily based on the hadith of the sheep that was slaughtered and roasted without the owner's permission. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that it be given to captives, which demonstrates that (1) the original owner's ownership is removed upon usurpation, and (2) the usurper cannot benefit before satisfying the owner (i.e., obtaining consent or paying compensation). The hadith is then presented in detail with its narration and chain criticism. The commentator defends the hadith's authenticity against Imam Abu Dawud's criticism, stating that the chain is sound through Asim ibn Kulayb from his father from a man of the Ansar, and that Asim and his father are trustworthy narrators. The discussion ends mid-sentence on page 348 regarding Humayd ibn al-Rabi' al-Khazzaz.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): The unlawful seizure of someone else's property without their consent.
ضمان (daman): Compensation or liability for the value or equivalent of the usurped property.
انتفاع (intifa'): Benefiting from a property, such as using or consuming it.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides an analogy due to a stronger evidence or public interest.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa cited in the passage from Samarqand, in the case of usurping and consuming food (e.g., chewing and swallowing), whose view is followed?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa's view that it is lawful with bodily obligation.
B) The Sahibayn's view that monetary compensation is required.
C) Hasan ibn Ziyad's view that it is permissible without compensation.
D) Imam Zufar's view that no compensation is needed.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position prohibits benefit before compensation, but within the school there are nuanced differences that affect fatwa in specific cases such as food consumption and planting.

The Owner's Option to Sell Usurped Dyed Cloth
Expansion of a ruling on usurped dyed cloth by Shaykh Abu 'Asma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Shaykh Abu 'Asma's ruling on the sale of dyed cloth and explain the proportional division of the sale proceeds.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the owner of a usurped and dyed cloth may sell it and split the price: one part for the cloth, one for the dye.

When a cloth is dyed without permission, the owner often faces a dilemma: keep the cloth and pay for the dye, or claim compensation for the cloth. Shaykh Abu 'Asma introduces a third option — sell the cloth and divide the proceeds fairly. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi school's flexibility in resolving property disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original issue
The original issue is usurpation (ghasb) of a white cloth that has been dyed red by the usurper. Understand the standard Hanafi options for the owner: either take the dyed cloth and pay for the dye (tamalluk) or hold the usurper liable for the value of the white cloth.
2
Identify the new option given by Abu 'Asma
Shaykh Abu 'Asma adds a third option: the owner may sell the dyed cloth. The sale proceeds are then divided proportionally—the owner receives the value of the white cloth, and the dyer receives the enhancement (ziyadah) from the dye.
This option is based on the owner's refusal to accept tamalluk of the dye.
3
Understand the rationale
The owner has the right not to accept ownership of the dye by paying its price. If the dyer is willing to be made liable (i.e., pay for the cloth), the sale method is a practical way to settle the claim without forcing either party to accept an unwanted transaction.
The dyer's readiness to be liable is key.
4
Extend to accidental dyeing
The ruling also applies when the cloth becomes dyed without the dyer's action (e.g., accidentally). In that case, the dyer is not at fault, so the owner cannot simply claim compensation for the cloth. The sale option becomes the primary method if the owner does not want to pay for the dye.
Accidental dyeing: no fault, so no liability for the cloth.
5
Contrast with usurpation
In the original usurpation case, the owner always has the right to hold the usurper liable for the white cloth (since usurpation is a wrong). Therefore, the sale method is not necessary; it is an additional option. In accidental dyeing, the sale method is the only non-compulsory way to recover value.
Usurpation: owner can always claim full cloth value from usurper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله قال ابو عصمة ... الخ شيخ ابو عصمہ سعد بن معاذ مروزی نے ( جو ابراہیم بن یوسف کے شاگرد ہیں ۔ اور وہ امام ابو یوسف کے شاگرد ہیں ) اصل مسئله يعني " و من غصب ثوباً احمر‘ میں کہا ہے کہ کپڑے کے مالک کو یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ وہ کپڑے کو فروخت کر دے اب اس کے ثمن میں کپڑے کا مالک اپنے سفید کپڑے کے حساب سے حصہ دار ہوگا۔ اور رنگ کا مالک زیادتی رنگ کے حساب سے حق دار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کپڑے کے مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ قیمت دے کر رنگ کی ملکیت منظور نہ کرے ۔ قوله ويتأتى هذا الخ لیکن شیخ ابو عصمہ کا قول مذکور صرف اصل مسئلہ ہی میں نہیں بلکہ اس صورت میں بھی جاری ہوتا ہے جب کپڑا رنگ والے کے کسی فعل کے بغیر خود بخو درنگ گیا ہو کیونکہ اس صورت میں اس کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ وہ صاحب صبح سے اس کا کوئی قصور نہ ہونے کے باوجود تا وان لے۔ پس جب کپڑے کا مالک تملک ثوب سے باز رہا اور صاحب صبغ کو جبر اضامن بنانا مستعد رہوا تو اس کو اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے لئے بیع کا طریقہ متعین ہو گیا۔ جب کہ کپڑے کا مالک رنگ کی قیمت دے کر تملک صبح سے راضی نہیں ہے۔ رہی غصب کی صورت سو اس میں کپڑے کا مالک اگر تملک صبغ سے باز رہے تو حق کی وصولیابی کے لئے بیع کا طریقہ متعین نہیں ۔ لان له تضمين الغاصب بالثوب الابيض
His statement: 'He said Abu 'Asma... etc.' Shaykh Abu 'Asma Sa'd ibn Mu'adh al-Marwazi (who is a student of Ibrahim ibn Yusuf, and he is a student of Imam Abu Yusuf) said in the original issue, i.e., 'Whoever usurps a red cloth', that the owner of the cloth also has the option to sell the cloth. Then in its price, the owner of the cloth will be a shareholder according to his white cloth, and the owner of the dye will be entitled according to the enhancement of the dye. Because the owner of the cloth has the option not to accept ownership of the dye by paying its price. His statement: 'And this applies... etc.' But the mentioned statement of Shaykh Abu 'Asma is not only in the original issue, but also applies in the case where the cloth becomes dyed by itself without any action of the dyer, because in that case the owner will not have the option to take compensation from the dyer despite there being no fault of his. So when the owner of the cloth refrains from taking ownership of the cloth and the owner of the dye is ready to be made liable, then the method of sale is determined for him to receive his right, since the owner of the cloth is not satisfied with paying the price of the dye and taking ownership. As for the case of usurpation, if the owner of the cloth refrains from taking ownership of the dye, the method of sale is not determined for receiving his right, because he has the option to hold the usurper liable for the white cloth.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling about a usurped cloth that has been dyed. Shaykh Abu 'Asma gives an alternative: besides the usual options (taking the dyed cloth and paying for the dye, or taking compensation for the cloth), the owner may choose to sell the cloth. The sale proceeds are then divided proportionally—the owner gets the value of the white cloth, and the dyer gets the enhancement added by the dye. This ruling applies even if the cloth became dyed without the dyer's act (e.g., accidentally). In that case, since the dyer is not a wrongdoer, the owner cannot simply take compensation for the cloth; instead, the sale method is used if the owner does not want to pay for the dye. In the original usurpation scenario, the owner can always hold the usurper liable for the value of the white cloth, so sale is not necessary.

Key Terms
تملك (tamalluk): Taking ownership of the dyed cloth by the owner, usually by paying the dyer for the dye.
زيادة (ziyadah): The enhancement in value due to the dye, which belongs to the dyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shaykh Abu 'Asma, what option does the owner of a usurped and dyed cloth have besides taking the cloth with compensation?
A) He can demand the cloth without paying anything
B) He can sell the cloth and divide the proceeds
C) He can force the dyer to remove the dye
D) He can abandon the cloth and claim full compensation

Key Takeaway
Shaykh Abu 'Asma's ruling provides a third option for the owner of a dyed cloth: sell it and split the proceeds, ensuring fair compensation for both parties.

Compensation for Roasted Sattu in Usurpation: Mithl vs Qimah
Commentary on ruling of compensation for mixed sattu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a fungible (mithli) becomes a non-fungible (qimi) due to transformation, and apply it to determine the correct compensation in usurpation.

Core Idea
Roasting sattu changes its nature, making it no longer mithli — compensation is by value, not by like.

In cases of usurpation, the type of compensation depends on whether the usurped item is fungible (mithli) or non-fungible (qimi). But what happens when the item undergoes a transformation, like roasting wheat into sattu? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and the intra-school difference on whether sattu remains mithli after roasting, drawing from the commentary on Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general ruling
The act is usurpation of sattu (roasted flour) which is then mixed with cloth. The general ruling is that compensation is wajib upon the usurper. The type of compensation (mithl or value) depends on the nature of the item.
2
Understand the mithli/qimi distinction
Sattu is ordinarily mithli (fungible) so its like (mithl) is owed. Cloth is qimi (non-fungible) so its market value (qimah) is owed. The passage focuses on sattu's classification after roasting.
Mithli items are those measured by weight, volume, or number with little variation; qimi items vary significantly in value.
3
Analyze the effect of roasting on sattu
Roasting alters the wheat components, creating a new substance (sawīq). According to Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Sabjabi, this change removes sattu from the category of mithliyyat, making it qimi. Therefore, value is due instead of mithl.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference and resolution
Some earlier scholars interpreted 'value' in Al-Mabsut to mean mithl itself. The preferred view is that 'value' is literal. The scholar resolves by stating that the mufta bihi is value, as roasting causes significant difference.
The tarjih authority is Sheikh Ala al-Din.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ستو کومسکہ میں خلط کرنے یا خود بخو د خلط ہو جانے میں بھی یہی دلیل جاری ہے۔ اور اس میں بھی شیخ ابو عصمتہ کا قول چل سکتا ہے صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ ستو متلی چیزوں میں سے ہے تو اس کے مثل کا تاوان دے گا اور کپڑا ایسی چیزوں میں سے ہے جس کا تاوان بقیمت ہوتا ہے لہذا اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گا۔
قوله وقال فی الاصل ... الخ - او پر معلوم ہوا کہ مسئلہ سویق میں ستو کے مثل کا تاوان دے گا۔ مگر اصل یعنی مبسوط میں مذکور ہے کہ سٹو کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بھوننے سے سٹو میں تفاوت ہو جاتا ہے تو وہ متلی نہیں رہتا ۔ شیخ علاؤالدین اسپیجابی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہی صحیح ہے۔ اس لئے کہ سویق ، بھنے ہوئے گیہوں کے اجزاء کا نام ہے۔ اور بھن جانے کی وجہ سے گیہوں ذوات الا مثال ہونے سے نکل جاتا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ مبسوط میں قیمت سے مراد شل ہی ہے۔ امام محمد نے اس کو قیمت سے اس لئے تعبیر کیا ہے کہ مثل مغصوب کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔
This same reasoning applies whether the sattu is mixed with cloth by the usurper or becomes mixed on its own. The statement of Sheikh Abu Isma can also apply here. The only difference is that sattu is among the mithli items, so he will pay its mithl (like), while cloth is among those items whose compensation is by value, so he is liable for its value. He (the commentator) said: 'And he said in Al-Asl ... etc.' - From this it becomes known that in the issue of sawiq (sattu), he will pay the mithl of sattu. But in Al-Asl, i.e., Al-Mabsut, it is mentioned that he is liable for the value of sattu, because roasting causes a difference in sattu, so it is no longer mithli. Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Sabjabi says this is correct, because sawiq is the name for roasted wheat components, and due to roasting, wheat leaves the category of mithliyat. Some mashayikh have said that by 'value' in Al-Mabsut, what is meant is the mithl itself. Imam Muhammad expressed it as 'value' because the mithl stands in place of the usurped item.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion within the chapter of usurpation (ghasb). It addresses the question of compensation when usurped sattu (roasted barley flour) is mixed with cloth. The commentator explains that if sattu is mixed with cloth, the general principle is that sattu, being a mithli (fungible) good, is compensated with its like (mithl), whereas cloth, a qimi (non-fungible) good, is compensated with its market value. However, a difference arises from the primary texts: in Al-Asl (the Mabsut of Imam Muhammad), it states that roasted sattu is liable for value, not mithl, because roasting alters its nature, taking it out of the category of mithliyyat. Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Sabjabi confirms this as the correct view. Some scholars try to reconcile by interpreting 'value' in Al-Mabsut as actually meaning the mithl, since the mithl is a substitute for the usurped item. The lesson shows how the classification of an item (mithli vs qimi) can change due to physical transformation, and the reliance on the authority of later Hanafi scholars in determining the operative ruling.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): Like or equivalent in kind and quality; compensation for a fungible (mithli) good.
قيمة (qimah): Market value; compensation for non-fungible goods or when mithl is unavailable.
سويق (sawīq): Sattu; roasted barley or wheat flour, a common food item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because sattu is a liquid that cannot be measured by weight
B) Because roasting changes its nature, removing it from the category of mithliyyat
C) Because it is mixed with cloth, which is qimi
D) Because the owner demands value

Key Takeaway
Transformation by roasting removes sattu from the category of mithliyyat, so compensation in usurpation is by value, not by like.

Deficient Ownership: Why the Usurper's Sale is Valid but Emancipation is Not
Ruling with proof: validity of usurper's sale vs. emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi distinction between the usurper's valid sale and invalid emancipation using the concept of milk nāqis and the analogy with the mukātib.

Core Idea
Deficient ownership suffices for sale but not for emancipation.

In Hanafi fiqh, the usurper (ghāṣib) acquires a peculiar form of ownership over the usurped property once he becomes liable for compensation. This ownership is not full; it is deficient (nāqis). This lesson unpacks a key passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah that demonstrates how this deficient ownership yields different rulings for sale and emancipation. The reasoning relies on two foundations: the nature of the usurper's ownership (established by necessity or attribution) and a qiyas (analogy) with the mukātib (a slave under contract of manumission). By the end, you'll see why the Hanafi school considers the sale valid but the emancipation invalid, and how this differs from the positions of other imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Ruling
Read the matn: the usurper sells a usurped slave; owner takes compensation (ḍamān) → sale valid. If instead he frees the slave and then compensates → emancipation invalid. Identify the two cases and the contrasting rulings.
The passage also notes Imam Ahmad agrees in one narration; others disagree.
2
Locate the Illa (Effective Cause)
The text explains that the usurper's ownership is deficient because it is established either by attribution (istinād) to the liability or by necessity (ḍarūrah). Analyze the reasoning: why does necessity arise? It is to prevent the substitute (value) and the original (slave) from coexisting in the same ownership. This deficiency means the ownership is only recognized for some purposes.
The deficiency manifests in that earnings belong to the usurper, but offspring belong to the original owner.
3
Apply the Qiyas with the Mukātib
The text draws an analogy (qiyas) with the ownership of a mukātib. A mukātib can buy and sell using his earnings but cannot emancipate another slave because his ownership is incomplete. Similarly, the usurper's deficient ownership is sufficient to effect a sale (transfer of ownership) but insufficient to effect emancipation (complete removal of ownership).
This qiyas is of type shabah (resemblance) because the common characteristic is milk nāqis.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The commentary mentions that Imam Shāfiʿī, Imam Mālik, and in another narration Imam Aḥmad hold the sale invalid. Their basis: the usurper's ownership is too weak for any transfer. Understand that the Hanafi response relies on the distinction between sale and emancipation and the sufficiency of deficient ownership for sale.
This is a thamarah al-khilāf: the practical difference is whether the buyer acquires valid ownership.
5
Summarize the Principle
Extract the general rule: milk nāqis (deficient ownership) is sufficient for acts that transfer ownership (like sale) but not for acts that completely terminate ownership (like ʿitq). This principle is rooted in the need to avoid joining badal and mubdal minhu, and is reinforced by the analogy with the mukātib.
Memorize the maxim: 'al-milk al-nāqis yanfaʿu fī al-bayʿ lā fī al-ʿitq'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاصب نے غلام غصب کر کے فروخت کر دیا تو مالک نے غاصب سے غلام کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب کی بیع جائز ہوگی اور اگر آزاد کر دیا تو قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اور آزاد کرنا درست نہ ہوگا
قال ومن غصب عبدا فباعه فضمنه المالک قیمته فقد جاز بيعه وان اعتقه ثم ضمن القيمة لم يجز عتقه لان الملك الثابت فيه ناقص لثبوته مستندا او ضرورة ولهذا يظهر فى حق الاكساب دون الاولاد والناقص يكفى لنفوذ البيع دون العتق كملك المكاتب
ترجمہ کسی نے غلام غصب کر کے فروخت کیا اور مالک نے اس سے اس کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب کی بیع جائز ہوگی اور اگر غلام کو آزاد کر دیا اور اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غلام میں جو ملکیت ثابت ہوئی تو وہ ناقص ہے اس کے مستند یا بضرورت ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لئے وہ کمائی کے حق میں ظاہر ہوتی ہے نہ کہ اولاد کے حق میں اور ناقص ملک نفاذ بیچ کے لئے کافی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ عشق کے لئے ملک مکاتب کی طرح۔
تشريح قوله ومن غصب عبدا.. الخ - ایک شخص نے کسی کا غلام غصب کر کے بیچ ڈالا ۔ اور مالک نے اس کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی ایک روایت میں امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور دوسری روایت میں امام احمد کے نزدیک بیج نافذ نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر غاصب نے غلام کو آزاد کر دیا پھر مالک نے تاوان لیا تو عتق نافذ نہ ہوگا ۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ ملک غاصب ناقص ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت بطریق استناد ہوتا ہے اور جو چیز بطریق استناد ثا بت ہو ۔ وہ من وجہ تاب لی مین وجہ غیر ثابت ہوتی ہے یا اس کا ثبوت بوجہ ضرورت ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ از روئے دلیل غصب کے ذریعہ سے ملک ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اس لئے کہ غصب عدوان محض ہے اور ملک ایک نعمت ہے غاصب کے لئے جو ملک ثابت ہو جاتی ہے وہ قضاء بالضمان کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ تا کہ ملک واحد میں بدل اور مبدل منہ دونوں جمع نہ ہو جائیں اور جو چیز ضرورۃ ثابت ہو، وہ بھی من وجہ ثابت اور من وجہ غیر ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اسی لئے ثبوت ملک کا ظہور صرف کمائی کے حق میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اولاد کے حق میں۔ چنانچہ اگر باندی غصب کی اور غاصب کے اداء ضمان سے پہلے اس نے کچھ کمائی کی۔ تو کمائی غاصب کی ہوگی ۔ اور اگر اداء ضمان سے پہلے اولاد ہوئی تو وہ مغصوب منہ کی ہوگی ۔ بہر کیف ملک غاصب ناقص ہوتی ہے اور ملک ناقص نفاذ بیچ کے لئے کافی ہوتی ہے نفاذ عشق کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوتی ۔ جیسے ملک مکاتب ہے کہ مکاتب اپنی کمائی میں خرید و فروخت کر سکتا ہے لیکن اپنی کمائی کا غلام آزاد نہیں کر سکتا۔
A person usurped a slave and then sold him; then the owner took the price from the usurper as compensation; then the usurper's sale is valid. But if he emancipated (the slave) and then became liable for the price, his emancipation is not valid. He said: 'And whoever usurps a slave and then sells him, and the owner makes him liable for the price, then his sale is valid. But if he emancipates him and then becomes liable for the price, his emancipation is not valid, because the ownership established in him is deficient (nāqis) due to its being established either by way of attribution (istinād) or by necessity (ḍarūrah). Therefore it appears regarding earnings but not regarding offspring. And the deficient suffices for the validity of sale but not for emancipation, like the ownership of a mukātib.' Translation: Someone usurped a slave and sold him, and the owner took the price as compensation, then the usurper's sale is valid. But if he freed the slave and then became liable for the price, his freeing is not valid. Because the ownership that is established in the slave is deficient due to its being by way of attribution or by necessity. Therefore it appears in the right of earnings, not in the right of offspring. And deficient ownership suffices for the validity of sale, not for emancipation, like the ownership of a mukātib. Explanation of his statement 'And whoever usurps a slave...' - A person usurped someone's slave and sold him, and the owner took the price as compensation, then the usurper's sale becomes valid. In one narration, Imam Ahmad also holds this. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and in another narration from Imam Ahmad, the sale is not valid. And if the usurper freed the slave and then the owner took compensation, the emancipation is not valid. The reason for the difference is that the usurper's ownership is deficient because its establishment is by way of attribution (istinād); something established by attribution is established in one aspect and not in another. Or its establishment is by necessity (ḍarūrah) because, rationally, ownership cannot be established through usurpation since usurpation is pure transgression and ownership is a blessing. Ownership established for the usurper is due to the necessity of adjudication with compensation (qaḍā' bil-ḍamān) so that the substitute and the original are not both combined in one ownership. And something established by necessity is also established in one aspect and not in another. Therefore the manifestation of ownership only appears regarding earnings, not regarding offspring. So if a slave-girl is usurped and earns something before the usurper pays compensation, the earnings belong to the usurper. But if offspring are born before payment, they belong to the person from whom she was usurped (the owner). In any case, the usurper's ownership is deficient, and deficient ownership suffices for the validity of sale but not for the validity of emancipation, like the ownership of a mukātib: the mukātib can buy and sell with his earnings, but he cannot free a slave from his earnings.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the effects of the usurper's ownership after he has paid or become liable for compensation. The ruling is stated in the Arabic matn: If a person usurps a slave and then sells him, and the owner subsequently takes the price as compensation (ḍamān), the sale is valid. However, if the usurper instead emancipates the slave and then becomes liable for the price, the emancipation is not valid. The commentary explains that this distinction is due to the nature of the usurper's ownership: it is deficient (nāqis) because it is established either by attribution (istinād) or by necessity (ḍarūrah). Ownership by attribution means the ownership is recognized only insofar as necessary to avoid combining the substitute (badal) and the original (mubdal minhu) in one hand. This deficient ownership is sufficient for sale (bayʿ) because sale is a transfer of ownership, and even a limited ownership can be transferred. But emancipation (ʿitq) is a complete removal of ownership, requiring full (kāmil) ownership to be effective. The commentary analogizes this to the ownership of a mukātib (a slave under a contract of manumission). The mukātib has a form of ownership over his earnings; he can sell and buy, but he cannot emancipate another slave because his ownership is incomplete. Similarly, the usurper can sell the slave he owns deficiently, but he cannot fully emancipate him. The commentary also notes that Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal agrees with the Hanafis in one narration, while Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and another narration from Imam Ahmad oppose, holding that the sale is not valid because the usurper's ownership is too weak.

Key Terms
ملک ناقص (Milk Nāqis): Deficient ownership; ownership that is valid for some purposes (like sale and benefiting from earnings) but not for others (like emancipation), due to being established by necessity or attribution rather than by full legal acquisition.
استناد (Istinād): Attribution; the concept that the usurper's ownership is attributed to the compensation liability, i.e., it exists only insofar as it is tied to the duty to pay the value. This makes it a conditional or derivative ownership.
قضاء بالضمان (Qaḍā' bil-Ḍamān): Adjudication with compensation; the legal mechanism by which the usurper's ownership is established through the requirement to compensate the owner, thereby avoiding the simultaneous existence of substitute and original in one ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider the usurper's sale valid but his emancipation invalid?
A) Because sale is a temporary transfer whereas emancipation is permanent.
B) Because the usurper's ownership is deficient, and deficient ownership suffices for sale but not for emancipation.
C) Because sale requires the owner's consent (which is absent) while emancipation does not.
D) Because the compensation only covers the value for sale, not for emancipation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates the usurper's sale because deficient ownership suffices for transfer, but invalidates emancipation because it requires full ownership.
